المرصد الثاني - المقصد الحادي عشر : الماهية تقبل الشركة دون التعين 
يتحصل كل منهما بالفصل والجنس الآخر، ولما كان كل منهما مبهماً لم يمكن أن يكون له مدخل في تحصيل الآخر إلا باعتبار تحصله في نفسه، فيلزم أن يكون تحصل كل منهما علة ناقصة لتحصل الآخر، فيلزم الدور.
المقصد الحادي عشر : الماهية تقبل الشركة دون التعين 
(الماهية) كالإنسان مثلاً تقبل الشركة أي لا تمنع من فرض اشتراكها وحملها على كثيرين دون التعين المخصوص؛ كتعين زيد مثلاً فإنه لا يمكن فرض اشتراكه بين أمور متعددة بالبديهة، فهو غيرها.
قوله: (لم يمكن أن يكون له مدخل إلخ) هذا مبني على أمرين: أحدهما أن الفصل علة فاعلية لتحصل الجنس وهو ظاهر والثاني أن المبهم لا يكون علة للمحصل، ولذا قيل: إن عدم جزء ما لا يجوز أن يكون علة لعدم الكل فإن تم تم وإلا فلا؛ إذ يجوز حينئذ أن يكون كل واحد من الجنسين باعتبار نفسه علة لتحصل الآخر، فيكون تحصلهما معاً فلا. قوله: (كالإنسان) أشار ذلك إلى أن المراد بالماهية الماهية النوعية بقرينة ذكر التعين معها. قوله: (وحملها إلخ) أشار بالعطف إلى أن الاشتراك الذي هو صفة المعلوم معناه الحمل لا المطابقة، فإنها صفة الصورة التي هي العلم.
تحقق حقيقة النوع به فلا نسلم توقف كل منهما على الآخر، بل الماهية المركبة من الأجزاء الثلاثة متوقفة عليها فلا دور. ولو صح ما ذكرتم لم تلتئم ماهية من ثلاثة أجزاء؛ إذ بأحدهما مع الآخر لا تتحصل الحقيقة بدون الثالث وبالعكس. بل نقول: الفصل لا يتحصل بدون الجنس، وإلا لتحصل النوع بدون الجنس فيلزم توقف كل منهما على الآخر في تحصله. وقد يوجه قولهم: وإلا لكان النوع متحققاً بدون الجنس الآخر بأن الجنس إذا تحصل صار هو من حيث إنه متحصل بما حصله نوعاً منه قطعاً، فإن ماهية النوع وهو الجنس المتحصل لا حقيقة له وراءه كما أشير إليه في أوائل هذا المقصد، فليس لما هو خارج من المتحصل الذي هو ذلك الجنس والمحصل الذي هو الفصل فرضاً مدخل في ماهية ذلك النوع، فيكون الجنس الآخر خارجاً عنها، فلا يكون جنساً لها، والتقدير بخلافه. وبهذا التوجيه يندفع البحث المذكور، لكن يتجه أن ذلك التقدير إنما يتم إذا كان الجنسان متساويين أما إذا كان أحدهما أشد إبهاماً كان يكون أعم مطلقاً فإنه يجوز أن يكون ذات الآخر مع الفصل محصلاً له، فلا يلزم الدور. قال الشارح في حواشي التجريد: فالأولى أن يقتصر على أن الماهية الواحدة لو كان لها جنسان في مرتبة واحدة لكان لها فصل محصل، فيتحصل كل منهما نوعاً على حدة، سواء كان الفصل واحداً أو متعدداً، فلا تكون الماهية نوعاً واحداً وماهية واحدة هذا خلف. قيل: وعلى هذا التقدير الأول منع ظاهر، وهو أنا لا نسلم أنه يتحصل به كل منهما نوعاً على حدة، وإنما يلزم ذلك أن لو لم يكن كلاهما مقوماً لنوع واحد على ما هو المفروض، ولا يخفى عليك اندفاعه بعد ما تحققت أن ماهية النوع هو الجنس المتحصل، وأن إنكار تحصل كل من الجنس بالفصل بمعنى زوال إبهامه مكابرة. قوله: (فيلزم الدور) قيل: لم لا يجوز أن يكون مفهومان في كل منهما إبهام من وجه، فيزول باجتماعهما إبهام كليهما، فيكون تحصل كل منهما باعتبار تحصل الآخر معه لا سابقاً عليه، ومثل ذلك يسمى دور معية، وهو غير باطل على ما قيل في الحيوان والناطق، وأنت خبير بأن هذا إنما يتصور إذا كان بين ذينك المفهومين عموم من وجه وفي جوازه في الماهيات الحقيقية كلام كما أشار إليه فيما سبق الآن. قوله: (فهو غيرها) هذا لازم لنتيجة القياس والنتيجة فهي غيره كما لا يخفى. قوله: (وجزء الموجود الخارجي موجود) فإن قلت: إذا كان التعين المخصوص موجوداً خارجياً، لم يستقم عدهم مطلق التعين من المعقولات الثانية؛ لوجود ما يطابقه في الخارج. قلت: أشرنا إلى جوابه في تحقيق أن الوجود من المعقولات فليتذكر. قوله: (والجواب: أن المراد بالمعين هو الشخص) إلخ فيه بحث: لأن مفهوم زيد وإن لم يكن مفهوم الإنسان وحده لكن لم لا يجوز أن يكون هو الإنسان المقيد بالعوارض الشخصية
وقد اختلف في التعين الذي هو غير الماهية وباعتباره معها يمتنع فرض اشتراكها هل هو وجودي أي موجود في الخارج أم لا؟ فذهب المحققون من العلماء إلى أنه وجودي؛ لأنه جزء المعين الموجود في الخارج، وجزء الموجود الخارجي موجود في الخارج بالضرورة. وقد قال بعضهم: يعني الكاتبي إن أردت بالمعين معروض التعين وحده، فلا نسلم أن التعين جزوه بل هو عارضه، ووجود المعروض في الخارج لا يستلزم وجود عارضه فيه، ألا ترى أن العمى العارض للموجودات الخارجية ليس موجوداً في الخارج أو المجموع المركب من العارض والمعروض فلا نسلم أنه أي المعين بهذا المعنى موجود، فإن من يمنع وجود التعين كيف يسلم أنه مع معروضه موجودان؟ بل الموجود عنده هو المعروض وحده. والجواب: أن المراد بالمعين الذي ادعينا وجوده هو الشخص
قوله (دون) التعين (المخصوص) قيد بذلك لأن المقصود بيان مغايرة الماهية النوعية للتعين العارض لها، وتقرير الاستدلال أن كل ماهية نوعية تقبل الشركة ولا شيء من التعين بقابل لها، فلا شيء من الماهية يتعين فثبت مغايرته لها بحسب الماهية سواء كان مغايراً لها في الوجود أو لا. قوله: (لأنه جزء المعين الموجود في الخارج فيه بحث لأنه إن جعل في الخارج ظرفاً للجزئية نمنع الصغرى، وإن جعل ظرفاً للوجود نمنع الكبرى، لأن الجزء الذهني للموجود الخارجي لا يجب أن يكون موجوداً في الخارج. قوله: (معروض التعين) أي الذات الذي يصدق عليه هذا المفهوم، وكذا في الشق الثاني؛ إذ لا معنى للترديد بين هذين المفهومين؛ إذ الدليل لا يحتملهما.
The Second Observance - The Eleventh Purpose: The Quiddity Accepts Commonality but Not Determination.
Each of them is actualized by the differentia and the other genus, and since each of them is ambiguous, it cannot have an entry in the actualization of the other except by virtue of its own actualization in itself, so it follows that the actualization of each of them is an incomplete cause for the actualization of the other, so circularity follows.
The Eleventh Purpose: The Quiddity Accepts Commonality but Not Determination.
(Al-māhiyya) like 'human' for example, accepts commonality, i.e., it does not prevent the supposition of its sharing and predication upon many, except (al-taʿayyun al-makhṣūṣ) the specific determination; like the determination of Zayd for example, for it is not possible to suppose its sharing among multiple things by necessity, so it is other than it.
His saying: (It cannot have an entry etc.) is based on two things: one is that the differentia is an efficient cause for the actualization of the genus, which is apparent, and the second is that the ambiguous cannot be a cause for the actualizer, hence it was said: The non-existence of a part cannot be a cause for the non-existence of the whole. If it is established, it is established; otherwise, no. For then it is permissible that each of the two genera, by virtue of itself, is a cause for the actualization of the other, so their actualization occurs together.
His saying: (like 'human') indicates that what is meant by al-māhiyya is the specific quiddity, by the context of mentioning determination with it.
His saying: (and its predication etc.) indicates by the conjunction that the commonality which is a property of the known means predication (al-ḥaml) not correspondence (al-muṭābaqa), for it is a property of the form which is knowledge.
The actualization of the reality of the species by it, so we do not grant the dependence of each of them on the other. Rather, the quiddity composed of three parts is dependent on them, so no circularity. And if what you mentioned were correct, a quiddity of three parts would not be composed; for with one of them along with the other, the reality is not actualized without the third, and vice versa. Rather, we say: The differentia is not actualized without the genus, otherwise the species would be actualized without the genus, necessitating the dependence of each of them on the other in its actualization. And it may be directed that their saying: 'Otherwise the species would be actualized without the other genus' is that when the genus is actualized, it becomes by virtue of being actualized by what actualized it a species, certainly. For the quiddity of the species, which is the actualized genus, has no reality beyond it, as was pointed out at the beginning of this purpose. So what is external to the actualized thing which is that genus and the actualizer which is the differentia has no entry in the quiddity of that species, so the other genus is external to it, thus it is not a genus for it. And the assumption is the contrary. By this direction the mentioned investigation is repelled. But it is directed that this assumption is only complete if the two genera are equal. If one of them is more ambiguous, being more general absolutely, then it is permissible that the essence of the other along with the differentia be an actualizer of it, so circularity does not occur.
The commentator said in the margins of al-Tajrīd: It is better to restrict to that the single quiddity, if it had two genera in one rank, it would have an actualizing differentia, so each of them would actualize a separate species, whether the differentia is one or multiple. So the quiddity would not be one species and one quiddity, which is a contradiction.
It was said: Based on this first estimation, there is an apparent objection, which is that we do not grant that each of them is actualized by the differentia as a separate species. Rather, that would be necessary if both were not constitutive of one species as is assumed. And it is not hidden from you that it is repelled after you have verified that the quiddity of the species is the actualized genus, and that denying the actualization of each of the two genera by the differentia in the sense of removing its ambiguity is stubbornness.
His saying: (so circularity follows). It was said: Why is it not permissible that there are two concepts each having ambiguity from one aspect, and by their conjunction the ambiguity of both is removed, so the actualization of each of them is by virtue of the actualization of the other with it, not prior to it. Such is called 'circularity of concomitance', and it is not invalid according to what was said regarding 'animal' and 'rational'. And you are aware that this is only conceivable if there is between the two concepts a generality from one aspect, and regarding its permissibility in real quiddities there is discussion as alluded to earlier.
His saying: (so it is other than it) - this is a necessary consequence of the syllogism, and the conclusion is that it is other than it, as is not hidden.
His saying: (and the part of the external existent is existent). If you say: If the specific determination is existent externally, then their counting of absolute determination among the secondary intelligibles would not be consistent, because there is something that corresponds to it in the external. I say: We have indicated its answer in the verification that existence is among the intelligibles, so let it be remembered.
His saying: (and the answer: that what is meant by the determinate is the person) etc. There is a discussion in it: because the concept of Zayd, even if it is not the concept of 'human' alone, yet why is it not permissible that it is 'human' qualified by personal accidents?
And there is disagreement regarding determination, which is other than the quiddity and by virtue of which along with it, the supposition of its sharing is impossible: is it existent (wujūdī), i.e., existing in the external, or not? So the verifiers (al-muḥaqqiqūn) among the scholars went to it being existent, because it is a part of the determinate (al-muʿayyan) existing in the external, and a part of the external existent is existent in the external necessarily. And some of them (meaning al-Kātibī) said: If you mean by al-muʿayyan the substrate (maʿrūḍ) of determination alone, then we do not grant that determination is a part of it, rather it is an accident (ʿāriḍ) of it. And the existence of the substrate in the external does not necessitate the existence of its accident in it. Do you not see that blindness which is accidental to external existents is not existent in the external? Or if you mean the composite (al-majmūʿ) composed of the accident and the substrate, then we do not grant that it (i.e., the determinate in this sense) is existent. For whoever denies the existence of determination, how can he grant that it and its substrate are two existents? Rather, what exists according to him is the substrate alone. And the answer: that what is meant by al-muʿayyan, whose existence we claimed, is the person (al-shakhṣ).
His saying: (without) determination (al-makhṣūṣ) is a restriction for that, because the objective is to demonstrate the otherness of the specific quiddity from the determination that is accidental to it. And the presentation of the proof is that every specific quiddity accepts commonality, and no determination is receptive to it, so no quiddity is determined, thus its otherness from it is established according to quiddity, whether it is other than it in existence or not.
His saying: (because it is a part of the determinate existing in the external) has an investigation in it, because if He makes the external a locus for the partiality, we deny the minor premise; and if He makes it a locus for existence, we deny the major premise, because the mental part of an external existent does not have to be existent in the external.
His saying: (the substrate of determination) i.e., the essence (dhāt) that is true of this concept, and likewise in the second branch; for there is no meaning to the disjunction between these two concepts, since the proof does not sustain them.
Source pages p. 86

Commentary
This passage is a combined definition and debate. It first defines the eleventh purpose (maqṣad): the quiddity (māhiyya) accepts commonality but not specific determination (taʿayyun). The author gives the example of 'human' as a quiddity that can be shared by many individuals, while a specific determination like 'Zayd' cannot be shared by multiple things by necessity. Thus, determination is other than the quiddity.

The commentary then addresses a potential circularity problem in the constitution of quiddity from genus and differentia. The argument is that if each (genus and differentia) is ambiguous, it cannot contribute to actualizing the other except by being actualized itself, leading to a vicious circle. The author responds by denying the premise that each depends on the other; rather, the quiddity composed of genus, differentia, and species is dependent on all parts, and the differentia is not actualized without the genus. He also discusses a case where the two genera are equal or one is more general, and a form of circularity (dawr maʿiyya) that is not invalid.

Later, the passage shifts to the debate about whether determination (taʿayyun) is existent (wujūdī) or not. The muḥaqqiqūn (verifiers) hold it is existent because it is a part of the external determinate thing. Al-Kātibī objects that if determination is an accident, its existence does not follow from the existence of the substrate, using blindness as an example. The answer clarifies that the intended 'determinate' is the person (shaKhṣ), which includes determination as a part. Further commentary analyzes the proof, noting potential pitfalls regarding the locus of partiality and existence.

The discussion underscores the metaphysical realism of the Ashʿarī tradition: determination is a real, external attribute, not merely a mental concept. The careful handling of circularity and the distinction between quiddity and determination are crucial for understanding individuation.

Key Terms
الدور (al-dawr, circularity)
الجنس (al-jins, genus)
الفصل (al-faṣl, differentia)
المبهم (al-mubham, ambiguous)
دور معية (dawr maʿiyya, circularity of concomitance)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All forms of circularity are logically invalid.
Correction: The passage discusses 'circularity of concomitance' (dawr maʿiyya) which may be acceptable in some cases, such as 'animal' and 'rational'.

Checkpoint
What is the condition under which the direction (tawjīh) that the other genus is external works?
A) When the two genera are equal
B) When one genus is more ambiguous
C) When the differentia is the sole cause
D) When the quiddity is composed of two parts

Key Takeaway
The actualization of genus and differentia cannot involve vicious circularity; a valid composition requires either independent actualization or a non-vicious circularity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Consider a belief you hold about Allah (e.g., His oneness) that you have built upon other beliefs. Is there any hidden circularity in your reasoning? How does the distinction between vicious and non-vicious circularity (dawr maʿiyya) challenge you to examine the foundations of your conviction?
?
The passage shows that even in logical analysis of quiddity, scholars debated subtle points. When you face ambiguity in matters of aqeedah, do you rush to resolve it or do you patiently analyze, aware that some circularities may be permissible? What does your approach reveal about your intellectual humility before divine truths?
?
If the differentia is like the specific quality that actualizes a genus, what is the 'differentia' that actualizes your faith? In other words, what specific belief or practice brings your general faith into concrete reality, and does it depend on something else that might create a circular dependency? Reflect on whether that circle is healthy or vicious.

Logic and Technical Terms
intermediate
6 min
The Debate on the Existence of Determination (Ta'ayyun)
Debates whether determination (taʿayyun) is existent in the external.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the disagreement about whether specific determination (taʿayyun) is an existent reality in the external world.

Core Idea
Is determination a real part of external things or just a mental accident?

This lesson addresses a key metaphysical question: does the determination that individuates a quiddity have external existence? The verifiers (muḥaqqiqūn) affirm it, while a position attributed to al-Kātibī denies it. The answer distinguishes between the person (shakhṣ) and the accident.

Guided Path
1
Read the debate passage
Read the passage starting from 'There is disagreement regarding determination...' and identify the two opposing views.
Note the terminology: 'wujūdī' (existent) vs. 'ʿāriḍ' (accident).
2
Understand the argument of the verifiers
The verifiers argue that determination is existent because it is a part of the external determinate (muʿayyan).
They use the premise that a part of an external existent is itself external.
3
Examine al-Kātibī's objection
Al-Kātibī objects that if determination is an accident (ʿāriḍ), its existence does not follow from the existence of the substrate, using blindness as an analogy.
This challenges the necessity of determination's external existence.
4
Consider the answer
The answer clarifies that the intended 'determinate' (al-muʿayyan) whose existence is claimed is the person (al-shakhṣ), which includes determination as part of its reality.
Thus, determination is not a mere accident but a constituent of the individual.

المرصد الثاني - المقصد الحادي عشر : الماهية تقبل الشركة دون التعين 
يتحصل كل منهما بالفصل والجنس الآخر، ولما كان كل منهما مبهماً لم يمكن أن يكون له مدخل في تحصيل الآخر إلا باعتبار تحصله في نفسه، فيلزم أن يكون تحصل كل منهما علة ناقصة لتحصل الآخر، فيلزم الدور.
المقصد الحادي عشر : الماهية تقبل الشركة دون التعين 
(الماهية) كالإنسان مثلاً تقبل الشركة أي لا تمنع من فرض اشتراكها وحملها على كثيرين دون التعين المخصوص؛ كتعين زيد مثلاً فإنه لا يمكن فرض اشتراكه بين أمور متعددة بالبديهة، فهو غيرها.
قوله: (لم يمكن أن يكون له مدخل إلخ) هذا مبني على أمرين: أحدهما أن الفصل علة فاعلية لتحصل الجنس وهو ظاهر والثاني أن المبهم لا يكون علة للمحصل، ولذا قيل: إن عدم جزء ما لا يجوز أن يكون علة لعدم الكل فإن تم تم وإلا فلا؛ إذ يجوز حينئذ أن يكون كل واحد من الجنسين باعتبار نفسه علة لتحصل الآخر، فيكون تحصلهما معاً فلا. قوله: (كالإنسان) أشار ذلك إلى أن المراد بالماهية الماهية النوعية بقرينة ذكر التعين معها. قوله: (وحملها إلخ) أشار بالعطف إلى أن الاشتراك الذي هو صفة المعلوم معناه الحمل لا المطابقة، فإنها صفة الصورة التي هي العلم.
تحقق حقيقة النوع به فلا نسلم توقف كل منهما على الآخر، بل الماهية المركبة من الأجزاء الثلاثة متوقفة عليها فلا دور. ولو صح ما ذكرتم لم تلتئم ماهية من ثلاثة أجزاء؛ إذ بأحدهما مع الآخر لا تتحصل الحقيقة بدون الثالث وبالعكس. بل نقول: الفصل لا يتحصل بدون الجنس، وإلا لتحصل النوع بدون الجنس فيلزم توقف كل منهما على الآخر في تحصله. وقد يوجه قولهم: وإلا لكان النوع متحققاً بدون الجنس الآخر بأن الجنس إذا تحصل صار هو من حيث إنه متحصل بما حصله نوعاً منه قطعاً، فإن ماهية النوع وهو الجنس المتحصل لا حقيقة له وراءه كما أشير إليه في أوائل هذا المقصد، فليس لما هو خارج من المتحصل الذي هو ذلك الجنس والمحصل الذي هو الفصل فرضاً مدخل في ماهية ذلك النوع، فيكون الجنس الآخر خارجاً عنها، فلا يكون جنساً لها، والتقدير بخلافه. وبهذا التوجيه يندفع البحث المذكور، لكن يتجه أن ذلك التقدير إنما يتم إذا كان الجنسان متساويين أما إذا كان أحدهما أشد إبهاماً كان يكون أعم مطلقاً فإنه يجوز أن يكون ذات الآخر مع الفصل محصلاً له، فلا يلزم الدور. قال الشارح في حواشي التجريد: فالأولى أن يقتصر على أن الماهية الواحدة لو كان لها جنسان في مرتبة واحدة لكان لها فصل محصل، فيتحصل كل منهما نوعاً على حدة، سواء كان الفصل واحداً أو متعدداً، فلا تكون الماهية نوعاً واحداً وماهية واحدة هذا خلف. قيل: وعلى هذا التقدير الأول منع ظاهر، وهو أنا لا نسلم أنه يتحصل به كل منهما نوعاً على حدة، وإنما يلزم ذلك أن لو لم يكن كلاهما مقوماً لنوع واحد على ما هو المفروض، ولا يخفى عليك اندفاعه بعد ما تحققت أن ماهية النوع هو الجنس المتحصل، وأن إنكار تحصل كل من الجنس بالفصل بمعنى زوال إبهامه مكابرة. قوله: (فيلزم الدور) قيل: لم لا يجوز أن يكون مفهومان في كل منهما إبهام من وجه، فيزول باجتماعهما إبهام كليهما، فيكون تحصل كل منهما باعتبار تحصل الآخر معه لا سابقاً عليه، ومثل ذلك يسمى دور معية، وهو غير باطل على ما قيل في الحيوان والناطق، وأنت خبير بأن هذا إنما يتصور إذا كان بين ذينك المفهومين عموم من وجه وفي جوازه في الماهيات الحقيقية كلام كما أشار إليه فيما سبق الآن. قوله: (فهو غيرها) هذا لازم لنتيجة القياس والنتيجة فهي غيره كما لا يخفى. قوله: (وجزء الموجود الخارجي موجود) فإن قلت: إذا كان التعين المخصوص موجوداً خارجياً، لم يستقم عدهم مطلق التعين من المعقولات الثانية؛ لوجود ما يطابقه في الخارج. قلت: أشرنا إلى جوابه في تحقيق أن الوجود من المعقولات فليتذكر. قوله: (والجواب: أن المراد بالمعين هو الشخص) إلخ فيه بحث: لأن مفهوم زيد وإن لم يكن مفهوم الإنسان وحده لكن لم لا يجوز أن يكون هو الإنسان المقيد بالعوارض الشخصية
وقد اختلف في التعين الذي هو غير الماهية وباعتباره معها يمتنع فرض اشتراكها هل هو وجودي أي موجود في الخارج أم لا؟ فذهب المحققون من العلماء إلى أنه وجودي؛ لأنه جزء المعين الموجود في الخارج، وجزء الموجود الخارجي موجود في الخارج بالضرورة. وقد قال بعضهم: يعني الكاتبي إن أردت بالمعين معروض التعين وحده، فلا نسلم أن التعين جزوه بل هو عارضه، ووجود المعروض في الخارج لا يستلزم وجود عارضه فيه، ألا ترى أن العمى العارض للموجودات الخارجية ليس موجوداً في الخارج أو المجموع المركب من العارض والمعروض فلا نسلم أنه أي المعين بهذا المعنى موجود، فإن من يمنع وجود التعين كيف يسلم أنه مع معروضه موجودان؟ بل الموجود عنده هو المعروض وحده. والجواب: أن المراد بالمعين الذي ادعينا وجوده هو الشخص
قوله (دون) التعين (المخصوص) قيد بذلك لأن المقصود بيان مغايرة الماهية النوعية للتعين العارض لها، وتقرير الاستدلال أن كل ماهية نوعية تقبل الشركة ولا شيء من التعين بقابل لها، فلا شيء من الماهية يتعين فثبت مغايرته لها بحسب الماهية سواء كان مغايراً لها في الوجود أو لا. قوله: (لأنه جزء المعين الموجود في الخارج فيه بحث لأنه إن جعل في الخارج ظرفاً للجزئية نمنع الصغرى، وإن جعل ظرفاً للوجود نمنع الكبرى، لأن الجزء الذهني للموجود الخارجي لا يجب أن يكون موجوداً في الخارج. قوله: (معروض التعين) أي الذات الذي يصدق عليه هذا المفهوم، وكذا في الشق الثاني؛ إذ لا معنى للترديد بين هذين المفهومين؛ إذ الدليل لا يحتملهما.
The Second Observance - The Eleventh Purpose: The Quiddity Accepts Commonality but Not Determination.
Each of them is actualized by the differentia and the other genus, and since each of them is ambiguous, it cannot have an entry in the actualization of the other except by virtue of its own actualization in itself, so it follows that the actualization of each of them is an incomplete cause for the actualization of the other, so circularity follows.
The Eleventh Purpose: The Quiddity Accepts Commonality but Not Determination.
(Al-māhiyya) like 'human' for example, accepts commonality, i.e., it does not prevent the supposition of its sharing and predication upon many, except (al-taʿayyun al-makhṣūṣ) the specific determination; like the determination of Zayd for example, for it is not possible to suppose its sharing among multiple things by necessity, so it is other than it.
His saying: (It cannot have an entry etc.) is based on two things: one is that the differentia is an efficient cause for the actualization of the genus, which is apparent, and the second is that the ambiguous cannot be a cause for the actualizer, hence it was said: The non-existence of a part cannot be a cause for the non-existence of the whole. If it is established, it is established; otherwise, no. For then it is permissible that each of the two genera, by virtue of itself, is a cause for the actualization of the other, so their actualization occurs together.
His saying: (like 'human') indicates that what is meant by al-māhiyya is the specific quiddity, by the context of mentioning determination with it.
His saying: (and its predication etc.) indicates by the conjunction that the commonality which is a property of the known means predication (al-ḥaml) not correspondence (al-muṭābaqa), for it is a property of the form which is knowledge.
The actualization of the reality of the species by it, so we do not grant the dependence of each of them on the other. Rather, the quiddity composed of three parts is dependent on them, so no circularity. And if what you mentioned were correct, a quiddity of three parts would not be composed; for with one of them along with the other, the reality is not actualized without the third, and vice versa. Rather, we say: The differentia is not actualized without the genus, otherwise the species would be actualized without the genus, necessitating the dependence of each of them on the other in its actualization. And it may be directed that their saying: 'Otherwise the species would be actualized without the other genus' is that when the genus is actualized, it becomes by virtue of being actualized by what actualized it a species, certainly. For the quiddity of the species, which is the actualized genus, has no reality beyond it, as was pointed out at the beginning of this purpose. So what is external to the actualized thing which is that genus and the actualizer which is the differentia has no entry in the quiddity of that species, so the other genus is external to it, thus it is not a genus for it. And the assumption is the contrary. By this direction the mentioned investigation is repelled. But it is directed that this assumption is only complete if the two genera are equal. If one of them is more ambiguous, being more general absolutely, then it is permissible that the essence of the other along with the differentia be an actualizer of it, so circularity does not occur.
The commentator said in the margins of al-Tajrīd: It is better to restrict to that the single quiddity, if it had two genera in one rank, it would have an actualizing differentia, so each of them would actualize a separate species, whether the differentia is one or multiple. So the quiddity would not be one species and one quiddity, which is a contradiction.
It was said: Based on this first estimation, there is an apparent objection, which is that we do not grant that each of them is actualized by the differentia as a separate species. Rather, that would be necessary if both were not constitutive of one species as is assumed. And it is not hidden from you that it is repelled after you have verified that the quiddity of the species is the actualized genus, and that denying the actualization of each of the two genera by the differentia in the sense of removing its ambiguity is stubbornness.
His saying: (so circularity follows). It was said: Why is it not permissible that there are two concepts each having ambiguity from one aspect, and by their conjunction the ambiguity of both is removed, so the actualization of each of them is by virtue of the actualization of the other with it, not prior to it. Such is called 'circularity of concomitance', and it is not invalid according to what was said regarding 'animal' and 'rational'. And you are aware that this is only conceivable if there is between the two concepts a generality from one aspect, and regarding its permissibility in real quiddities there is discussion as alluded to earlier.
His saying: (so it is other than it) - this is a necessary consequence of the syllogism, and the conclusion is that it is other than it, as is not hidden.
His saying: (and the part of the external existent is existent). If you say: If the specific determination is existent externally, then their counting of absolute determination among the secondary intelligibles would not be consistent, because there is something that corresponds to it in the external. I say: We have indicated its answer in the verification that existence is among the intelligibles, so let it be remembered.
His saying: (and the answer: that what is meant by the determinate is the person) etc. There is a discussion in it: because the concept of Zayd, even if it is not the concept of 'human' alone, yet why is it not permissible that it is 'human' qualified by personal accidents?
And there is disagreement regarding determination, which is other than the quiddity and by virtue of which along with it, the supposition of its sharing is impossible: is it existent (wujūdī), i.e., existing in the external, or not? So the verifiers (al-muḥaqqiqūn) among the scholars went to it being existent, because it is a part of the determinate (al-muʿayyan) existing in the external, and a part of the external existent is existent in the external necessarily. And some of them (meaning al-Kātibī) said: If you mean by al-muʿayyan the substrate (maʿrūḍ) of determination alone, then we do not grant that determination is a part of it, rather it is an accident (ʿāriḍ) of it. And the existence of the substrate in the external does not necessitate the existence of its accident in it. Do you not see that blindness which is accidental to external existents is not existent in the external? Or if you mean the composite (al-majmūʿ) composed of the accident and the substrate, then we do not grant that it (i.e., the determinate in this sense) is existent. For whoever denies the existence of determination, how can he grant that it and its substrate are two existents? Rather, what exists according to him is the substrate alone. And the answer: that what is meant by al-muʿayyan, whose existence we claimed, is the person (al-shakhṣ).
His saying: (without) determination (al-makhṣūṣ) is a restriction for that, because the objective is to demonstrate the otherness of the specific quiddity from the determination that is accidental to it. And the presentation of the proof is that every specific quiddity accepts commonality, and no determination is receptive to it, so no quiddity is determined, thus its otherness from it is established according to quiddity, whether it is other than it in existence or not.
His saying: (because it is a part of the determinate existing in the external) has an investigation in it, because if He makes the external a locus for the partiality, we deny the minor premise; and if He makes it a locus for existence, we deny the major premise, because the mental part of an external existent does not have to be existent in the external.
His saying: (the substrate of determination) i.e., the essence (dhāt) that is true of this concept, and likewise in the second branch; for there is no meaning to the disjunction between these two concepts, since the proof does not sustain them.
Source pages p. 86

Commentary
This passage is a combined definition and debate. It first defines the eleventh purpose (maqṣad): the quiddity (māhiyya) accepts commonality but not specific determination (taʿayyun). The author gives the example of 'human' as a quiddity that can be shared by many individuals, while a specific determination like 'Zayd' cannot be shared by multiple things by necessity. Thus, determination is other than the quiddity.

The commentary then addresses a potential circularity problem in the constitution of quiddity from genus and differentia. The argument is that if each (genus and differentia) is ambiguous, it cannot contribute to actualizing the other except by being actualized itself, leading to a vicious circle. The author responds by denying the premise that each depends on the other; rather, the quiddity composed of genus, differentia, and species is dependent on all parts, and the differentia is not actualized without the genus. He also discusses a case where the two genera are equal or one is more general, and a form of circularity (dawr maʿiyya) that is not invalid.

Later, the passage shifts to the debate about whether determination (taʿayyun) is existent (wujūdī) or not. The muḥaqqiqūn (verifiers) hold it is existent because it is a part of the external determinate thing. Al-Kātibī objects that if determination is an accident, its existence does not follow from the existence of the substrate, using blindness as an example. The answer clarifies that the intended 'determinate' is the person (shaKhṣ), which includes determination as a part. Further commentary analyzes the proof, noting potential pitfalls regarding the locus of partiality and existence.

The discussion underscores the metaphysical realism of the Ashʿarī tradition: determination is a real, external attribute, not merely a mental concept. The careful handling of circularity and the distinction between quiddity and determination are crucial for understanding individuation.

Key Terms
التعين (al-taʿayyun, determination)
الوجودي (al-wujūdī, existent)
المحققون (al-muḥaqqiqūn, verifiers)
الكاتبي (al-Kātibī)
المعين (al-muʿayyan, the determinate)
الشخص (al-shakhṣ, person)
العارض (al-ʿāriḍ, accident)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Determination is a purely mental concept (maʿqūl thānī) with no external reality.
Correction: The verifiers argue that determination is existent in the external as a part of the person (shakhṣ).

Checkpoint
According to the verifiers (muḥaqqiqūn), why is determination existent?
A) Because it is a secondary intelligible
B) Because it is a part of the substrate (maʿrūḍ)
C) Because it is a part of the determinate existing in the external
D) Because all accidents exist externally

Key Takeaway
According to the verifiers, determination is a real part of the external person, not merely a mental concept.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Your identity is not a bundle of accidents; it is a real determination from Allah. Do you live as if your uniqueness is a divine gift, or do you downplay it? Pause now and thank Allah for making you distinct.
?
The verifiers argue determination exists externally. When you look at another person, do you see only a generic human, or do you recognize the real, individual determination that makes them irreplaceable? How would this change your treatment of others?
?
If determination were merely mental, then your past actions and personal history would have no real anchor. Do you ground your accountability to Allah in the fact that you are a real, determined individual? Reflect on this and commit to living in light of your unique responsibility.

Essence and Individuation Are Mentally Distinguished
The author uses analogy to explain the mental distinction between essence and individuation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how essence (māhiyya) and individuation (ta‘ayyun) are mentally distinguished but united in external existence, using the analogy of genus and species.

Core Idea
Essence and individuation are one in reality, two in the mind.

This passage offers a powerful analogy to clarify the ontological status of quiddity and its individual instantiations. By comparing the relationship of quiddity to its individualizers to the relationship of genus to species, the author argues that the composition is mental, not external. Understanding this distinction is crucial for avoiding errors about predication and the nature of individuals.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once to get the flow, then read the English translation. Notice the parallel structure between the two comparisons.
The passage uses a clear 'just as... so too' structure.
2
Analyze the analogy
Identify the two halves of the analogy: genus to specific differences, and quiddity to individualizers. Understand how each pair is related in the mind versus in external reality.
The key point is that in both cases, the two are united externally and distinguished only mentally.
3
Grasp the conclusion
Understand why the author concludes that there is only one existent (the personal identity) and why the alternative would undermine predication.
The example of 'human quiddity' and the individual person illustrates the point.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واعلم أن نسبة الماهية إلى المشخصات كنسبة الجنس إلى الفصول فكما أن الجنس مبهم في العقل يحتمل ماهيات متعددة ولا تعين لشيء منها إلا بانضمام فصل إليه؛ وهما متحدان ذاتاً وجعلاً ووجوداً في الخارج، ولا يتمايزان إلا في الذهن كذلك الماهية النوعية تحتمل هويات متعددة، ولا تعين لشيء منها إلا بمشخص ينضم إليها، وهما متحدان في الخارج ذاتاً وجعلاً ووجوداً، ومتمايزان في الذهن فقط. فليس في الخارج موجود هو الماهية الإنسانية مثلا، وموجود آخر هو التشخص حتى يتركب منهما فرد منها، وإلا لم يصح حمل الماهية على أفرادها، بل ليس هناك إلا موجود واحد أعني الهوية الشخصية إلا أن العقل يفصلها إلى ماهية نوعية وتشخص كما يفصل الماهية النوعية إلى الجنس والفصل.
Know that the relationship of quiddity (al-māhiyya) to individualizers (al-mushakhaṣṣāt) is like the relationship of genus (al-jins) to specific differences (al-fuṣūl). For just as the genus is vague in the mind, admitting multiple quiddities, and no determination occurs for any of them except by the addition of a specific difference, and they are united in essence, positing, and existence in the external world, and are distinguished only in the mind, so too the specific quiddity admits multiple identities, and no determination occurs for any of them except by an individualizer that is joined to it; and they are united in the external world in essence, positing, and existence, and are distinguished only in the mind. Thus, there does not exist in the external world an existent that is the human quiddity, for example, and another existent that is the individuation, so that an individual would be composed from them; otherwise, the predication of the quiddity on its individuals would not be sound. Rather, there is only one existent, namely the personal identity (al-huwiyya al-shakhṣiyya), except that the mind separates it into a specific quiddity and an individuation, just as it separates the specific quiddity into genus and specific difference.
Source pages p. 89

Commentary
This passage presents an argument by analogy to show that the composition of an individual from quiddity (māhiyya) and individuation (ta‘ayyun) is mental, not external. The author compares the relationship between quiddity and its individual instantiations to the relationship between genus and species. Just as genus is vague in the mind and becomes determinate only by adding a specific difference, and in external reality genus and difference are one in essence, positing, and existence, and are distinguished only in the mind, similarly the specific quiddity (e.g., humanity) is indeterminate among multiple individuals and becomes determinate only by adding an individuator. In external reality, the quiddity and the individuator are one entity; there is no separate existence of quiddity apart from the individual. If there were, then predication of the quiddity on its individuals would be invalid. Rather, there is only one existing thing, the personal identity (al-huwiyya al-shakhṣiyya), but the mind abstracts from it the specific quiddity and the individuation, just as it abstracts genus and difference from the species.

Key Terms
الماهية (quiddity)
التعين (individuation)
المشخص (individuator)
الجنس (genus)
الفصل (specific difference)
الهوية الشخصية (personal identity)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that the composition of essence and individuation is a real external composition, i.e., that a person is made of two distinct parts: a universal quiddity and an individuating factor.
Correction: The author argues that quiddity and individuation are one in external existence; they are distinguished only mentally. If they were separate, predication of the quiddity on individuals would not be valid.

Checkpoint
What does the analogy of genus and species illustrate?
A) Essence and individuation are separate in external reality.
B) Essence and individuation are mentally distinguished, but one in existence.
C) Individuation is an external addition to essence.
D) Genus always exists as a separate universal.

Key Takeaway
Quiddity and individuation are not two separate things in reality; they are one existent that the mind distinguishes, just as it distinguishes genus and species difference.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you look at yourself, do you ever treat your 'humanity' as something separate from your own unique person? How does the author's argument challenge that spontaneous tendency?
?
If your quiddity and individuation are one existent in reality, what does that mean about the permanence and reality of your personal identity? Is it merely a mental abstraction?
?
In your relationship with Allah, do you ever think of yourself as 'just a human' (quiddity) rather than this specific individual (individuation)? How might this lesson correct an impersonal view of your servanthood?

Specific Differences vs. Individuators
Distinguishing specific differences from individuators and establishing the exclusive external existence of individuals.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the crucial distinction between specific differences (fuṣūl) and individuators (mushakhiṣṣāt), and why only individual entities exist in external reality.

Core Idea
Specific differences create universal concepts; individuators produce only sensory particulars.

In classical Islamic metaphysics, a key question is how universal concepts relate to particular individuals. The author here sharpens the distinction between the 'specific differences' that define species and the 'individuators' that pick out particular instances. He argues that only individuals have external existence, while universals are mental abstractions.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice how the author contrasts the two types of things.
2
Identify the key contrast
Look for how specific differences produce universal images in the mind, while individuators only produce sensory particulars.
3
Understand the conclusion
The author concludes that individuals are distinguished by their identities, not individuators, and that only individuals exist externally.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم أشار إلى الفرق بقوله : ( بيد أنه لا يحصل من كل مشخص صورة في العقل مغايرة للصورة الأخرى الحاصلة من مشخص آخر؛ لأن المشخصات أمور جزئية لا ترتسم صورها في ذات النفس، بل في آلاتها، فكذا صورة الماهية المتشخصة إنما ترتسم في الآلة، ولا تتناولها إلا الإشارة الحسية أو الوهمية، بخلاف صور الفصول وما يتحصل بها من الأنواع فإنها أمور كلية يتحصل منها في العقل صور متغايرة، وبالجملة فالفصول تحصل ماهيات متخالفة تنطبع في العقول، والمشخصات تحصل هويات ترتسم في الحواس مع كون الماهية واحدة، ( والأشخاص تمايزها في الوجود الخارجي بهوياتها)، أي بذواتها لا بمشخصاتها كما يتبادر إليه الوهم؛ إذ لا تمايز في هذا الوجود بين الماهية والمشخص. ومن ههنا ظهر أن لا وجود في الخارج إلا للأشخاص، وأما الطبائع والمفهومات الكلية، فينتزعها العقل من الأشخاص تارة من ذواتها وأخرى من الأعراض المكتنفة بها بحسب استعدادت مختلفة واعتبارات شتى. فمن قال بوجود الطبائع في الخارج، إن أراد به أن الطبيعة الإنسانية مثلا بعينها موجودة في الخارج مشتركة بين أفرادها، لزمه أن يكون الأمر
Then he pointed to the difference by saying: 'But it is not the case that from each individualizer a form is obtained in the mind that is different from the other form obtained from another individualizer, because individualizers are particular things whose forms are not imprinted in the soul itself, but in its instruments. Thus the form of the individuated quiddity is imprinted only in the instrument, and is only apprehended by sensory or imaginal reference, unlike the forms of specific differences and the species obtained through them, for they are universal things from which various forms are obtained in the mind. In sum, specific differences produce diverse quiddities that are impressed in the intellects, while individualizers produce identities that are imprinted in the senses while the quiddity is one. And individuals are distinguished in external existence by their identities, i.e., by their essences, not by their individualizers, as would occur to imagination; for there is no distinction in this existence between quiddity and individualizer. From here it becomes clear that there is no existence in the external world except for individuals. As for universal natures and concepts, the mind extracts them from individuals sometimes from their essences and sometimes from the accompanying accidents according to different dispositions and various considerations. Whoever asserts the existence of universal natures in the external world, if he means that human nature, for example, as such exists externally common among its individuals, then he must...'
Source pages p. 89

Commentary
This passage first distinguishes the function of specific differences (fuṣūl) from individuators (mushakhiṣṣāt) in the mind. Specific differences produce universal mental images that can be applied to many, while individuators are particular material things that do not imprint their images in the soul itself but in the sensory faculties. Therefore, the image of an individuated quiddity is perceived only by sensory or imaginary reference. Then the author concludes that individuals in external existence are distinguished by their essences (huwiyyāt), not by individuators, since there is no distinction between quiddity and individuator in external reality. From this, it becomes clear that nothing exists externally except individuals; universal natures are abstracted by the mind from individuals. Whoever claims that universals exist externally as common between individuals would be committed to an absurdity that is then elaborated.

Key Terms
الفصول (specific differences)
المشخصات (individuators)
الذهن (mind)
الخارج (external world)
الطبائع الكلية (universal natures)
الهوية (identity)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think individuators produce universal concepts like specific differences.
Correction: The author shows that individuators only yield sensory particular images, not universal mental images.

Checkpoint

A) They are abstract concepts.
B) They are particular material things that imprint in sensory faculties.
C) They are mental constructions.
D) They are identical to specific differences.

Key Takeaway
Only individual entities exist in the external world; universal natures are concepts abstracted by the mind from individuals.

Quiddity and Individuation: The Foundation of Particulars
Defines quiddity's capacity for sharing and explains the distinction between particular and universal forms, concluding that only individuals exist externally.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how quiddity can be shared in the mind while individuals are distinguished by their very identities in external existence.

Core Idea
Individuals are distinguished by their essences, not by added individuators.

The author begins by establishing a crucial distinction: quiddity can be shared among many individuals, but only in the mind. In external reality, each individual is uniquely identified by its own identity, which is inseparable from its quiddity. This lesson introduces the key concepts and sets the stage for the refutation of universal natures.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to get an overview of the main claims about quiddity, individuation, and the distinction between particular and universal forms.
Pay attention to the contrast between forms imprinted in instruments versus in the mind.
2
Identify the two types of forms
Notice that particular forms (from individuators) are imprinted in the instrument (senses or estimative faculty), while universal forms (from differentiae) are imprinted in the mind.
3
Understand the identity of individuals
The passage states that individuals are distinguished by their identities (essences), not by individuators. In external existence, quiddity and individuator are united, so distinction is by the essence itself.
This refutes the idea that individuation comes from an added attribute.
4
Grasp the conclusion
The author concludes that only individuals exist externally; universal natures and concepts are mental abstractions derived from individuals.
This conclusion is the basis for the upcoming refutation of external universals.

جزئية لا ترتسم صورها في ذات النفس، بل في آلاتها، فكذا صورة الماهية المتشخصة إنما ترتسم في الآلة، ولا تتناولها إلا الإشارة الحسية أو الوهمية، بخلاف صور الفصول وما يتحصل بها من الأنواع فإنها أمور كلية يتحصل منها في العقل صور متغايرة، وبالجملة فالفصول تحصل ماهيات متخالفة تنطبع في العقول، والمشخصات تحصل هويات ترتسم في الحواس مع كون الماهية واحدة، ( والأشخاص تمايزها في الوجود الخارجي بهوياتها)، أي بذواتها لا بمشخصاتها كما يتبادر إليه الوهم؛ إذ لا تمايز في هذا الوجود بين الماهية والمشخص. ومن ههنا ظهر أن لا وجود في الخارج إلا للأشخاص، وأما الطبائع والمفهومات الكلية، فينتزعها العقل من الأشخاص تارة من ذواتها وأخرى من الأعراض المكتنفة بها بحسب استعدادت مختلفة واعتبارات شتى. فمن قال بوجود الطبائع في الخارج، إن أراد به أن الطبيعة الإنسانية مثلا بعينها موجودة في الخارج مشتركة بين أفرادها، لزمه أن يكون الأمر

بشرط شيء محمول عليه .

واحد من الثلاثة منه. وبهذا يندفع توهم لزوم انحصار كل ماهية في شخص واحد، بناء على توهم أن الماهية إذ كانت متحدة مع المشخص ذاتاً، وكان تميز الأشخاص بذواتها لكون المقتضي للتعين هوية الماهية نعم يرد أن يقال عدم الامتياز بين الماهية والمشخص في الخارج لا يستلزم أن تكون هوية الماهية عين هوية المشخصات؛ لجواز أن يكون صدقه بأن لا يكون للمشخصات هوية خارجية؛ لكونها من المعقولات الثانية على قياس ما حققه الشارح في بحث

قوله : ( غير قابل للاشتراك فيه بديهة دعوى البديهة في محل النزاع غير مسموعة، كيف وقد صرح الشارح قدس سره في حواشي المطالع بأن صاحب الكشف والمطالع منعا منافاة التشخص لعروض الاشتراك ؟ . ثم إن أراد بقوله : مع قطع النظر عن غيره قطع النظر عن كل ما يغاير نفسه حتى الوجود الخارجي أيضا، فلا نسلم كونه متعينا في حد ذاته وإن أراد قطع النظر عن كل ما يغايره سوى الوجود فالملازمة ،مسلمة، لكن الطبيعة الموجودة متعددة بحسب تعدد أشخاصها، فلا يلزم منه منه حصول شيء واحد بالشخص في أمكنة متعددة ولا اتصافه بصفات متضادة، وسيجي تفصيله. قوله : ( صورته العقلية) أي صورته المدركة بالعقل، سواء كانت حاصلة في ذاته أو في آلاته. قوله : ( بمعنى المطابقة لكثيرين معنى المطابقة لكثيرين أن لا يحصل من تعقل كل
واحد منها أثر متجدد.
قوله : (لا بمعنى الاشتراك أي الحقيقي فإن الشركة الحقيقية ممتنعة العروض للشيء في الخارج والذهن معاً.
قوله : ( بالفعل) متعلق بقوله ،اتصف وإنما قيد بذلك لأن الصورة المذكورة تتصف بالمطابقة بالقوة، بأن جردها العقل عن المشخصات الخارجية .
لا تكون متعينة عندهم ولك أن تقول : مراده أن كل موجود إذا لوحظ اتصافه بالوجود كان متعيناً، والهيولى إنما توجد مع مقارنة الصورة، والحق أن الجمع بين القول باتحاد هيولى العناصر شخصاً وامتناع وجود الكلي الطبيعي في الخارج، واشتراكه بين كثيرين محل تأمل، سيما إذا كان الشخص عبارة عن الماهية المقيدة بالتشخص كالهيولى بالنسبة إلى الصورة إلا أن يؤول كلامهم في الهيولى بما سنذكره في المقصد الثاني عشر.
Second Observatory - Eleventh Topic: The quiddity accepts sharing without individuation. A particular (thing) does not have its forms imprinted in the essence of the soul, but in its instruments. Likewise, the form of the individuated quiddity is only imprinted in the instrument, and only sensory or estimative indication reaches it, unlike the forms of the differential and what is obtained through them of species, for they are universal matters from which are obtained in the intellect different forms. In sum, the differential yield contrary quiddities that are impressed in minds, and the individuators yield identities that are imprinted in the senses while the quiddity is one. (And individuals are distinguished in external existence by their identities), i.e., by their essences, not by their individuators as the estimative faculty would immediately suppose; for there is no distinction in this existence between the quiddity and the individuator. From here it is apparent that there is no existence in the external world except for individuals. As for natures and universal concepts, the intellect abstracts them from individuals—sometimes from their essences and other times from the accidents surrounding them, according to different predispositions and various considerations. Whoever says that natures exist externally—if he intends that human nature, for example, itself exists externally shared among its individuals, then it would require that [the matter be] one [and the same] person in multiple places, qualified by opposite attributes; because every external existent is such that when considered in itself, disregarding other than it, it is determined in itself, not admitting sharing in it self-evidently. And if he intends that there exists in the external world something which, when conceived in its essence, its mental form is qualified by universality in the sense of corresponding to many, not in the sense of actual sharing, then that is also false, for, as just mentioned, the external existent is determined in itself, so its particular form cannot correspond to many. And if he intends that there exists in the external world something which, when conceived and stripped of its individuators, yields in the intellect a universal form, then that is precisely the doctrine that says: no. (Commentary follows explaining each phrase, including objections and answers regarding prime matter, the self-evidence of determination, and the nature of universality.)
Source pages p. 90

Commentary
This passage is a definition-and-proof section. It first defines the topic: quiddity accepts sharing without individuation. It explains that particular things are not directly represented in the soul but through instruments; likewise, the form of an individuated quiddity is imprinted only in the instrument and is only accessible via sensory or estimative indication. Species forms, however, are universal and produce different mental images. The author then states that individuals are distinguished in external existence by their identities (essences), not by individuators, because in external existence there is no separation between quiddity and individuator. From this, the author concludes that only individuals exist externally; universal natures and concepts are mental abstractions from individuals. The passage then examines three possible interpretations of the claim that natures exist externally. The first interpretation (that a nature like humanity itself exists externally shared among individuals) is refuted because it would lead to one individual being in multiple places with opposite attributes, but external existents are necessarily determined and cannot be shared. The second interpretation (that an external existent’s mental form corresponds to many without actual sharing) is rejected because the external thing’s form is particular and cannot correspond to many. The third interpretation (that stripping an external existent of its individuators yields a universal mental concept) is accepted as the correct view, that the universal is only in the mind. The commentary then addresses objections: the example of prime matter (hayula) as being one person but in multiple places is refuted because prime matter becomes fragmented with the advent of forms and does not remain a single person without qualification. The claim that determination is self-evident is challenged, as some scholars deny that individuation prevents sharing. The passage ends with a note that the combination of saying prime matter of elements is one person and denying the existence of the natural universal in the external world is problematic, especially if person means quiddity restricted by individuation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The belief that quiddity and individuator are separate in external reality, and that individuation is an added attribute.
Correction: In external existence, quiddity and individuator are united; there is no distinction between them. Individuals are distinguished by their very identities (essences), not by separate individuators.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what distinguishes individuals in external existence?
A) Their individuators, which are separate from their essences
B) Their identities (essences)
C) Their material composition
D) The accidents surrounding them

Key Takeaway
Individuals are distinguished by their very identities, and only individuals exist externally; universals are mental abstractions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that only individuals like you and me exist externally, or do you sometimes treat abstract concepts like 'justice' or 'faith' as if they have their own independent reality? How does this lesson correct that tendency in your daily life?
?
When you think of Allah's attribute of 'Mercy', do you conceive of it as a real existent separate from Allah? How does the lesson's conclusion that only individuals exist externally reshape your understanding of Allah's attributes being identical with His essence?
?
Consider your own existence: are you just a generic 'human being' or a unique individual distinguished by your very essence? How does this realization affect your sense of personal accountability before Allah, knowing that your identity is not a mere accident but your very self?

Refuting Universal Natures: The Three Interpretations
Refutes external universal natures by examining three interpretations and addressing objections about prime matter and self-evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why universal natures cannot exist externally, through the refutation of the first two interpretations and the acceptance of the third, along with key objections.

Core Idea
An external existent is determined in itself; it cannot be shared or correspond to many.

Having established that only individuals exist externally, the author now tackles the claim that universal natures have external reality. He presents three possible interpretations: actual sharing, mental correspondence without sharing, and abstraction after stripping individuators. The first leads to absurdities, the second is false, and the third is accepted as the correct view. This lesson examines each interpretation and the objections raised, including those concerning prime matter and self-evidence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and translation, which includes the three interpretations and the objections. The text contains some interwoven commentary; focus on the main argument.
The passage is dense; take your time.
2
Identify the three interpretations
Listen for the three 'if he intends' (إن أراد) statements. Each presents a different way to understand the claim that natures exist externally.
3
Understand the refutation of the first interpretation
The first interpretation (actual sharing) is refuted because it would require one individual to be in multiple places with opposite attributes, which is impossible since each external existent is self-determined.
The author argues this is self-evident (بديهة).
4
Understand the refutation of the second interpretation
The second (mental correspondence without actual sharing) is false because a particular form of an external existent cannot correspond to many individuals; it is determined to its own particularity.
5
Accept the third interpretation
The third (abstraction) is accepted as the correct view: universals are mental products, not external realities. This is the position of the author.

Second Observatory - Eleventh Topic: The quiddity accepts sharing without individuation. A particular (thing) does not have its forms imprinted in the essence of the soul, but in its instruments. Likewise, the form of the individuated quiddity is only imprinted in the instrument, and only sensory or estimative indication reaches it, unlike the forms of the differential and what is obtained through them of species, for they are universal matters from which are obtained in the intellect different forms. In sum, the differential yield contrary quiddities that are impressed in minds, and the individuators yield identities that are imprinted in the senses while the quiddity is one. (And individuals are distinguished in external existence by their identities), i.e., by their essences, not by their individuators as the estimative faculty would immediately suppose; for there is no distinction in this existence between the quiddity and the individuator. From here it is apparent that there is no existence in the external world except for individuals. As for natures and universal concepts, the intellect abstracts them from individuals—sometimes from their essences and other times from the accidents surrounding them, according to different predispositions and various considerations. Whoever says that natures exist externally—if he intends that human nature, for example, itself exists externally shared among its individuals, then it would require that [the matter be] one [and the same] person in multiple places, qualified by opposite attributes; because every external existent is such that when considered in itself, disregarding other than it, it is determined in itself, not admitting sharing in it self-evidently. And if he intends that there exists in the external world something which, when conceived in its essence, its mental form is qualified by universality in the sense of corresponding to many, not in the sense of actual sharing, then that is also false, for, as just mentioned, the external existent is determined in itself, so its particular form cannot correspond to many. And if he intends that there exists in the external world something which, when conceived and stripped of its individuators, yields in the intellect a universal form, then that is precisely the doctrine that says: no. (Commentary follows explaining each phrase, including objections and answers regarding prime matter, the self-evidence of determination, and the nature of universality.)
Source pages p. 90

Commentary
This passage is a definition-and-proof section. It first defines the topic: quiddity accepts sharing without individuation. It explains that particular things are not directly represented in the soul but through instruments; likewise, the form of an individuated quiddity is imprinted only in the instrument and is only accessible via sensory or estimative indication. Species forms, however, are universal and produce different mental images. The author then states that individuals are distinguished in external existence by their identities (essences), not by individuators, because in external existence there is no separation between quiddity and individuator. From this, the author concludes that only individuals exist externally; universal natures and concepts are mental abstractions from individuals. The passage then examines three possible interpretations of the claim that natures exist externally. The first interpretation (that a nature like humanity itself exists externally shared among individuals) is refuted because it would lead to one individual being in multiple places with opposite attributes, but external existents are necessarily determined and cannot be shared. The second interpretation (that an external existent’s mental form corresponds to many without actual sharing) is rejected because the external thing’s form is particular and cannot correspond to many. The third interpretation (that stripping an external existent of its individuators yields a universal mental concept) is accepted as the correct view, that the universal is only in the mind. The commentary then addresses objections: the example of prime matter (hayula) as being one person but in multiple places is refuted because prime matter becomes fragmented with the advent of forms and does not remain a single person without qualification. The claim that determination is self-evident is challenged, as some scholars deny that individuation prevents sharing. The passage ends with a note that the combination of saying prime matter of elements is one person and denying the existence of the natural universal in the external world is problematic, especially if person means quiddity restricted by individuation.

Key Terms
طبيعة
كلية
اشتراك
تعين
هيولى

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The belief that universal natures exist externally as shared realities or as mental forms that correspond to many without abstraction.
Correction: Universal natures do not exist externally; they are mental abstractions from individuals. An external existent is determined in itself and cannot be shared or correspond to many.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why can't human nature itself exist externally shared among individuals?
A) Because human nature is too abstract to be material.
B) Because each external existent is determined in itself and cannot be shared by many individuals.
C) Because the intellect abstracts universals only from accidents, not from essences.
D) Because individuals are distinguished by individuators, not by their identities.

Key Takeaway
External existents are particular and determined; universal natures exist only as mental abstractions.

?
هل تعامل الناس على أنهم مجرد أفراد من نوع (مثل 'طالب' أو 'أجنبي') متناسيًا حقيقة أن كل واحد منهم متعين في ذاته لا يشاركه فيه غيره؟ كيف يمكنك أن ترى كل شخص ككيان فريد غير قابل للاشتراك؟

The Quiddity Accepts Sharing Without Determination – Refuting One Entity in Multiple Places
Sanusi refutes the idea that quiddity's sharing means a single entity in multiple places.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the notion that 'one entity in multiple places' is an incorrect interpretation of quiddity sharing, and why every external existent is inherently determined and unshareable.

Core Idea
No external existent can be shared by intuition – each is necessarily determined in itself.

This lesson addresses a common misinterpretation of the statement that the quiddity (essence) accepts sharing without determination. Some might think this means a single entity can exist in multiple places with opposite attributes. The author firmly refutes this by appealing to the very nature of external existence: every existing thing, when considered in itself, is uniquely determined and not intrinsically shareable.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage slowly, then the translation. Note that the author states the topic and immediately refutes a misunderstanding.
2
Understand the key terms
Focus on 'quiddity' (الماهية), 'sharing' (الشركة), 'determination' (التعين), and 'one in person' (الواحد بالشخص). These are essential to grasp the argument.
3
Follow the refutation
Notice the logical move: the author claims that every external existent is determined in itself, thus cannot be shared by intuition. Ask yourself why this leads to the rejection of the interpretation.
4
Connect to the broader topic
Realize that this refutation sets the stage for a proper understanding of how quiddity can be 'shared' – it is about universality, not a single particular in multiple locations.
The lesson is a cornerstone for the rest of the discussion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المرصد الثاني - المقصد الحادي عشر : الماهية تقبل الشركة دون التعين. الواحد بالشخص في أمكنة متعددة متصفاً بصفات متضادة؛ لأن كل موجود خارجي فهو بحيث إذا نظر إليه في نفسه مع قطع النظر عن غيره كان متعيناً في حد ذاته غير قابل للاشتراك فيه بديهة.
The second observatory - the eleventh topic: The quiddity accepts sharing without determination. (It is) the one in person in multiple places, described with opposite attributes; because every external existent is such that when it is considered in itself, disregarding others, it is determined in its essence, not sharable by intuition.
Source pages p. 91

Commentary
This passage defines the topic and immediately refutes a possible misinterpretation. It states that the quiddity accepts sharing without determination. Then it explains what is meant: that one and the same entity could be in multiple places simultaneously with opposite attributes. The refutation is that every external existent, when considered in itself apart from others, is necessarily determined in its essence and cannot be shared intuitively. The claim that it can be shared is thus refuted by the very nature of existence.

Key Terms

Correction: The author clarifies that every external existent is determined in itself and cannot be shared, so this interpretation is false.

Checkpoint

D) Because the quiddity is abstract and cannot be placed.

Key Takeaway
The quiddity's 'sharing without determination' does not mean a single particular exists in multiple places; every external existent is uniquely determined and cannot be shared.

The passage refutes the idea that one entity can be in multiple places with opposite attributes. Yet in your life, do you try to hold contradictory positions or serve two masters? Where might you be attempting to 'be in multiple places' spiritually? Will you surrender this impossibility and accept the singular, determined path that God has placed you on?

Refuting the Second Interpretation: Mental Image Matching Many
Refutes the interpretation that an external existent's mental image is universal through matching many

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the second interpretation of universality (that a mental image matches many individuals) is false.

Core Idea
No mental image of a determined external existent can truly match many.

The author continues to examine interpretations of universality. Here, he addresses the idea that when we conceive an external thing, its mental image becomes universal by matching many individuals. He refutes this by appealing to the determinate nature of external existents.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
First, read the Arabic passage and its literal English translation to grasp the author's claim.
Notice the two conditions: matching many vs. actual sharing.
2
Identify the interpretation being refuted
The interpretation states that an external existent's mental image is universal in the sense of matching many individuals, not by actual sharing.
3
Understand the refutation
The author argues that the external existent is determined in itself, so its specific image cannot match many. This is a direct logical refutation.
Recall the previous lesson's point about determination.
4
Connect to the broader argument
This refutation reinforces that universality cannot reside in mental images of particular external things, supporting the author's overall position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن أراد أن في الخارج موجوداً إذا تصور هو في ذاته اتصف صورته العقلية بالكلية بمعنى المطابقة لكثيرين لا بمعنى الاشتراك بينهما بالفعل، فهو أيضاً باطل؛ لما آنفاً مر أن الموجود الخارجي متعين في حد نفسه، فلا تكون صورته المخصوصة مطابقة لكثيرين.

The author clarifies that 'matching many' means that thinking of each individual does not produce a new effect, and 'not actual sharing' means that the sharing is potential. He refutes this by reiterating that the external existent is determined, so its specific image cannot match many.

Third Interpretation: Identifying the Natural Universal
Identifies the third interpretation with the doctrine of the natural universal.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the third interpretation—that stripping a concrete existent yields a universal mental image—is identified with the doctrine of the natural universal.

Core Idea
Mental abstraction of universals is simply the natural universal revisited.

In this passage, the author presents a third possible interpretation of the universal. Some might think that by 'universal' we mean a mental image derived from an external existent after stripping away its individuating features. The author immediately points out that this is not a new position—it is exactly the doctrine of the natural universal. This lesson clarifies that identification and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Start by reading the Arabic sentence once, then the literal translation. Notice the structure: a conditional 'if' followed by a conclusion.
The author uses a concise style typical of kalam texts.
2
Understand the process described
The interpretation involves taking an external existent, mentally stripping its individuators (mushakhkhasat), and obtaining a universal image (surah kulliyyah) in the mind. Reflect on what 'stripping individuators' means—abstracting away particular characteristics.
This is a mental act, not a physical change.
3
Recognize the identification with natural universal
The author says 'that is exactly the doctrine of those who affirm the existence of the natural universal.' Understand that the natural universal (al-kulli al-tabi'i) is a well-known position in Islamic thought. This interpretation does not introduce a new view; it simply restates an old one.
The natural universal is considered to exist in external particulars as their common nature.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن أراد أن في الخارج موجوداً إذا تصور وجرد عن مشخصاته حصل منه في العقل صورة كلية فذلك بعينه مذهب القائلين بوجود الكلي الطبيعي.
And if he meant that in the external there is an existent such that when it is conceived and stripped of its individuators, a universal image results from it in the mind, then that is exactly the doctrine of those who affirm the existence of the natural universal.
Source pages p. 91

This passage presents a third interpretation: that when an external existent is mentally stripped of its individuators (mushakhkhasat), a universal image (surah kulliyyah) results. The author immediately identifies this with the doctrine of the natural universal (kulli tabi'i), which is a well-known position in kalam. This serves as a transition to the ensuing discussion about the natural universal.

Objection from the Hyle of the Elements and Its Response
Refutes the objection that the hyle of the elements contradicts the earlier principle.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the hyle of the elements can be one in person yet exist in multiple places with opposite attributes, and why this does not contradict rational principles.

Core Idea
Personal unity does not require indivisibility when division is by form, not by essence.

We now encounter an objection that seems to challenge the earlier rule: if nothing can be in two places at once, how can the hyle of the elements be one in person yet spread across different places with opposite attributes? The objection is not frivolous; it draws on a real philosophical concept. In this passage, the author resolves the apparent contradiction by clarifying the nature of the hyle's unity.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
Begin by reading the objection that claims the hyle of the elements is a counterexample to the earlier principle. Notice how it states that the hyle is one in person yet occurs in multiple places with opposite attributes.
The objection is introduced with 'وما قيل' (And what is said).
2
Understand the author's response
Next, read the author's response. He argues that the hyle is divided by the occurrence of specific forms, so each part occupies a place and has different attributes. However, since the hyle in itself is neither connected nor disconnected, this division does not affect its personal unity.
Key phrase: 'لما لم تكن في ذاتها متصلة ولا منفصلة' (since it is in itself neither connected nor disconnected).
3
Reflect on the analogy
The author gives an analogy: a single piece of wood colored with multiple colors. Consider how the wood remains one piece despite having different colors in different parts. This illustrates the concept of personal unity despite division.
The analogy helps to visualize the abstract concept.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وما قيل : هذا منقوض بهيولى العناصر، فإنها مع كونها واحدة بالشخص حاصلة في أمكنة متعددة متصفة بصفات متضادة ،فوهم، لأن هيولاها تبعضت بورود الصور النوعية فحصل كل بعض منها في مكان واتصف بصفات متضادة لصفات البعض، إلا أنها لما لم تكن في ذاتها متصلة ولا منفصلة لم يضر ذلك التبعيض في وحدتها الشخصية، كخشبة واحدة ملونة بألوان متعددة.
And what is said: This is refuted by the hyle of the elements, for it, while being one in person, occurs in multiple places described with opposite attributes, is a misunderstanding, because its hyle was divided by the occurrence of specific forms, so each part occurred in a place and was described with attributes opposite to the attributes of the other part, but since it is in itself neither connected nor disconnected, that division did not harm its personal unity, like a single piece of wood colored with multiple colors.
Source pages p. 91

Commentary
This passage presents an objection against the earlier refutation using the example of the hyle (hyle of the elements). The objection claims that the hyle is one in person yet exists in multiple places with opposite attributes, which would seem to contradict the claim that no single entity can be in multiple places. The response is that this is a misunderstanding: the hyle is divided by the occurrence of specific forms, so each part occupies its own place and has different attributes. However, because the hyle is in itself neither connected nor disconnected, this division does not affect its personal unity, similar to a single piece of wood painted with multiple colors that remains one piece.

Key Terms

العناصر
الصور النوعية
التبعيض
الوحدة الشخصية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Thinking that the hyle of the elements being one in person means it is indivisible and cannot have parts in different places.
Correction: The hyle can be divided by the occurrence of forms, and because it is neither inherently connected nor disconnected, this division does not affect its personal unity.

Checkpoint

B) The hyle is divided by specific forms, but its personal unity remains because it is neither connected nor disconnected.
C) The hyle is not really one; it only appears one.
D) The hyle's unity is metaphorical.

Key Takeaway
The hyle of the elements retains personal unity despite being divided by forms, because its essence is not intrinsically connected or disconnected.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
