Why Intuition Is Not a Valid Proof in This Dispute
Rejects intuitive status of determination by citing authorities.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why appealing to intuition is rejected as a proof in theological disputes, and how the author uses scholarly consensus to support this position.

Core Idea
Intuition cannot settle a disputed matter; authority matters.

The passage opens with a direct critique of those who claim that the determination of external existents is intuitively obvious. The author argues that such an appeal to intuition is unacceptable in a point of contention, especially when respected scholars have explicitly denied the premise. This lesson unpacks that rejection and its basis.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic sentence and its translation. Notice the strong language: 'not accepted' (غير مسموعة) at the beginning.
2
Identify the claim being rejected
The claim is that it is intuitive (بديهة) that an external existent is not sharable. The author says this is not a valid claim in a disputed matter.
Remember that intuition (بديهة) means self-evident knowledge.
3
Note the evidence against the claim
The author cites the commentator (الشارح) who states that two authorities (صاحب الكشف والمطالع) denied that individuation (التشخص) prevents sharing (عروض الاشتراك). This shows scholarly disagreement.
This is a direct rebuttal: if those scholars denied the link, it cannot be intuitive.
4
Reflect on the method
Ask yourself: What does this teach about theological argumentation? It shows that appeals to obviousness are not enough—actual reasoned positions matter.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( غير قابل للاشتراك فيه بديهة دعوى البديهة في محل النزاع غير مسموعة، كيف وقد صرح الشارح قدس سره في حواشي المطالع بأن صاحب الكشف والمطالع منعا منافاة التشخص لعروض الاشتراك ؟ . ثم إن أراد بقوله : مع قطع النظر عن غيره قطع النظر عن كل ما يغاير نفسه حتى الوجود الخارجي أيضا، فلا نسلم كونه متعينا في حد ذاته وإن أراد قطع النظر عن كل ما يغايره سوى الوجود فالملازمة ،مسلمة، لكن الطبيعة الموجودة متعددة بحسب تعدد أشخاصها، فلا يلزم منه منه حصول شيء واحد بالشخص في أمكنة متعددة ولا اتصافه بصفات متضادة، وسيجي تفصيله.
His statement: 'not sharable by intuition' — claiming intuition in a disputed matter is not accepted. How so, when the commentator (may his secret be sanctified) stated in the margins of al-Matali' that the author of al-Kashshaf and al-Matali' both denied that individuation prevents the occurrence of sharing? Then if he meant by 'disregarding others' disregarding everything other than itself including even external existence, then we do not concede that it is determined in itself. And if he meant disregarding everything other than itself except existence, then the implication is granted, but the existing nature is multiple according to the multiplicity of its individuals, so it does not necessitate the occurrence of one thing in person in multiple places nor its description with opposite attributes, and its detailed discussion will come.
Source pages p. 91

Commentary
This passage critically examines the claim that it is intuitive (bidahah) that external existents are determined and not sharable. The author points out that appealing to intuition is not accepted in a disputed matter, especially since the commentator in his glosses on al-Matali' stated that both the author of al-Kashshaf and al-Matali' denied that individuation prevents the occurrence of sharing. Then he provides a detailed analysis of the phrase 'disregarding others' (ma' qat' al-nazar 'an ghayrihi). If it means disregarding everything other than itself, including even existence, then the claim of determination is not conceded. If it means disregarding everything except existence, then the implication is granted, but then the nature exists in multiple individuals, so it does not lead to one thing being in multiple places nor opposite attributes. The detailed discussion is promised later.

Key Terms
بديهة
محل النزاع
التشخص
عروض الاشتراك

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Believing that the determination of external existents is so obvious that it cannot be disputed.
Correction: The author argues that appealing to intuition is invalid in a disputed matter, especially when respected scholars have explicitly denied the premise.

Checkpoint
Why does the author reject the claim that it is intuitive that an external existent is not sharable?
A) Because intuition is always false in philosophy.
B) Because the commentator says that two scholars denied that individuation prevents sharing.
C) Because external existents can be sharable in some sense.
D) Because the claim is based on a misreading of the text.

Key Takeaway
Appealing to intuition does not settle a theological dispute; one must engage with the reasoned arguments of earlier authorities.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Think of a recent disagreement you had about a religious matter. Did you rely on your own intuition or 'common sense' without checking what scholars have said? How does this lesson challenge you to change that habit?
?
Is there a theological belief you hold so strongly that you consider it 'obvious' or 'undeniable'? Are you willing to honestly examine whether it might be disputed among qualified scholars? What would it mean for your faith if you had to give up that certainty?
?
When you hear a scholar disagreeing with a view you intuitively believe, do you feel defensive? Can you commit, starting today, to suspending your intuition in favor of seeking authoritative evidence, even when it feels uncomfortable?

Two Interpretations of 'Disregarding Others'
Disambiguates 'disregarding others' into two cases and refutes each.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two possible interpretations of the phrase 'disregarding others' in the debate about determination, and why neither leads to the opponent's conclusion.

Core Idea
How you interpret 'disregarding others' changes the logical outcome.

The author now analyzes the key phrase 'disregarding others' (مع قطع النظر عن غيره) used by the opponent. He shows that whether it excludes everything including existence, or excludes everything except existence, neither interpretation supports the claim that an external existent is inherently determined and not sharable. This lesson unpacks this nuanced disambiguation.

Guided Path
1
Read the full passage
Read the Arabic passage and translation carefully. Notice the conditional structure: 'If he meant... then...' and 'If he meant... then...'.
The passage is an extended conditional analysis.
2
Identify the two interpretations
First interpretation: 'disregarding others' means disregarding everything other than itself, including external existence. Second interpretation: it means disregarding everything other than itself except existence.
The difference is whether existence is excluded or included.
3
Analyze the logical implications
For the first interpretation, the author denies the conclusion of determination. For the second, he concedes the implication but shows it leads to multiplicity, not a single determined thing.
Notice the key word 'فلا نسلم' (we do not concede) and 'الملازمة مسلمة' (the implication is granted).
4
Reflect on the broader argument
The author shows that even if we accept the opponent's premise, the conclusion does not follow. The nature exists in multiple individuals, so it does not produce one thing in multiple places or opposite attributes.
This is a classic refutation by disambiguation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( غير قابل للاشتراك فيه بديهة دعوى البديهة في محل النزاع غير مسموعة، كيف وقد صرح الشارح قدس سره في حواشي المطالع بأن صاحب الكشف والمطالع منعا منافاة التشخص لعروض الاشتراك ؟ . ثم إن أراد بقوله : مع قطع النظر عن غيره قطع النظر عن كل ما يغاير نفسه حتى الوجود الخارجي أيضا، فلا نسلم كونه متعينا في حد ذاته وإن أراد قطع النظر عن كل ما يغايره سوى الوجود فالملازمة ،مسلمة، لكن الطبيعة الموجودة متعددة بحسب تعدد أشخاصها، فلا يلزم منه منه حصول شيء واحد بالشخص في أمكنة متعددة ولا اتصافه بصفات متضادة، وسيجي تفصيله.
His statement: 'not sharable by intuition' — claiming intuition in a disputed matter is not accepted. How so, when the commentator (may his secret be sanctified) stated in the margins of al-Matali' that the author of al-Kashshaf and al-Matali' both denied that individuation prevents the occurrence of sharing? Then if he meant by 'disregarding others' disregarding everything other than itself including even external existence, then we do not concede that it is determined in itself. And if he meant disregarding everything other than itself except existence, then the implication is granted, but the existing nature is multiple according to the multiplicity of its individuals, so it does not necessitate the occurrence of one thing in person in multiple places nor its description with opposite attributes, and its detailed discussion will come.
Source pages p. 91

Commentary
This passage critically examines the claim that it is intuitive (bidahah) that external existents are determined and not sharable. The author points out that appealing to intuition is not accepted in a disputed matter, especially since the commentator in his glosses on al-Matali' stated that both the author of al-Kashshaf and al-Matali' denied that individuation prevents the occurrence of sharing. Then he provides a detailed analysis of the phrase 'disregarding others' (ma' qat' al-nazar 'an ghayrihi). If it means disregarding everything other than itself, including even existence, then the claim of determination is not conceded. If it means disregarding everything except existence, then the implication is granted, but then the nature exists in multiple individuals, so it does not lead to one thing being in multiple places nor opposite attributes. The detailed discussion is promised later.

Key Technical Terms: Mental Image, Matching Many, and Actual Sharing
Defines the technical terms used in the discussion of universality and mental images

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the precise meanings of four key terms used in discussions of universality: mental image, matching many, actual sharing, and the distinction between potential and actual matching.

Core Idea
Mental images match many individuals potentially, not actually.

In this concise passage, the author clarifies the technical vocabulary essential for the debate on universals. He explains what a 'mental image' is, what it means for a concept to 'match many' individuals, and why 'actual sharing' is impossible. Pay close attention to the distinction between potential and actual matching.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the English translation to get a sense of the definitions.
The passage is dense with technical terms; reading both versions helps.
2
Identify the four terms defined
Look for the definitions of 'mental image', 'matching many', 'actual sharing', and the qualification 'in actuality'.
Each term is introduced with 'قوله' (his statement).
3
Understand the definition of mental image
Note that mental image is the image perceived by the intellect, whether in the intellect itself or in its instruments (like the brain).
4
Distinguish matching many from actual sharing
Matching many means no renewed effect from conceiving each individual, while actual sharing (real sharing) is impossible for a thing in both external and mental existence.
This is a crucial distinction for the discussion of universals.
5
Grasp the qualification 'in actuality'
Understand that the image is described with matching potentially (bil-quwwah) when stripped of external individuators, not actually matching multiple individuals.
This clarifies that mental universals are potential, not actual.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( صورته العقلية) أي صورته المدركة بالعقل، سواء كانت حاصلة في ذاته أو في آلاته. قوله : ( بمعنى المطابقة لكثيرين معنى المطابقة لكثيرين أن لا يحصل من تعقل كل واحد منها أثر متجدد. قوله : (لا بمعنى الاشتراك أي الحقيقي فإن الشركة الحقيقية ممتنعة العروض للشيء في الخارج والذهن معاً. قوله : ( بالفعل) متعلق بقوله ،اتصف وإنما قيد بذلك لأن الصورة المذكورة تتصف بالمطابقة بالقوة، بأن جردها العقل عن المشخصات الخارجية.
His statement: 'his mental image' means his image perceived by the intellect, whether it occurs in his essence or in his instruments. His statement: 'in the sense of matching many' – the meaning of matching many is that no renewed effect occurs from the intellection of each one of them. His statement: 'not in the sense of actual sharing' – i.e., real sharing, for real sharing is impossible for a thing in both external existence and the mind together. His statement: 'in actuality' is attached to his statement 'is described' – and he only qualified it thus because the mentioned image is described with matching potentially, by the intellect stripping it of external individuators.
Source pages p. 91

Commentary
This passage provides clarifications of key terms used in the second interpretation. First, 'his mental image' (surah 'aqliyyah) is defined as the image perceived by the intellect, whether it occurs in the intellect itself or in its instruments (like the brain). Second, 'matching many' (mutabaqah li-kathirin) means that no new effect results from conceiving each individual, indicating a unified concept. Third, 'not in the sense of actual sharing' (la bi-ma'na al-ishtirak) means real sharing is impossible for any thing in both external and mental existence simultaneously. Finally, 'in actuality' (bil-fi'l) qualifies that the image is described with matching potentially (bil-quwwah) when the intellect strips it of external individuators, not actually matching many individuals in the external world.

مطابقة
اشتراك حقيقي
بالفعل
بالقوة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that 'matching many' means the mental image actually shares reality with many external objects.
Correction: The passage clarifies that 'matching many' means no new effect from each intellection, while 'actual sharing' is impossible for a thing in both mind and external.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the difference between 'matching many' and 'actual sharing'?
A) Matching many is potential, actual sharing is real.
B) Matching many means no renewed effect from intellection of each, while actual sharing is impossible for a thing in both mind and external.
C) Matching many is a property of the intellect, actual sharing is of the external world.
D) There is no difference; they are synonymous.

Key Takeaway
The key distinction is that mental images match many individuals potentially, not actually, while real sharing in both mind and external is impossible.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you conceive a concept in your mind—like justice, mercy, or even Allah's oneness—do you ever mistake your mental image for the reality itself? How has this lesson's distinction between potential matching and actual sharing uncovered a hidden arrogance in your intellectual assumptions? What will you do today to humble your mind before the truth, recognizing that your concepts are only tools?
?
The passage says matching many means 'no renewed effect occurs from the intellection of each one.' This means your mental concept of, say, 'knowledge' applies uniformly to many instances without you feeling a new shock each time. But reflect: have you become so comfortable with your mental images of faith—prayer, fasting, tawhid—that you no longer feel the weight of each individual instance? Will you today engage with one specific act of worship as if for the first time, refusing to let your mind's potential matching rob you of awe?
?
Real sharing between mind and external existence is impossible, the text insists. Yet we often speak as if our mental beliefs perfectly mirror external truth. Where in your life do you treat your own understanding as if it literally shares existence with Allah's reality? How can you use this lesson to guard against the sin of equating your mental constructs with divine truth, and in what concrete situation will you apply this guard today?

Reflection on the Hyle's Unity and the Natural Universal
Questions the consistency of personal unity of hyle and denial of natural universal.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why combining the personal unity of the hyle with the denial of the natural universal's external existence is problematic, and how the author suggests a resolution through interpretation.

Core Idea
The hyle's unity and the natural universal's non-existence are in tension, requiring careful interpretation.

In this passage, the author raises a critical question about the consistency of two commonly held positions in Aristotelian physics and metaphysics. He points out an apparent contradiction between affirming the personal unity of the hyle (prime matter) and denying the existence of the natural universal in external reality. This sets up a difficulty that requires careful interpretation.

Guided Path
1
Understand the two positions
Identify the two claims being combined: (a) the hyle of the elements is one in person, and (b) the natural universal cannot exist externally and be shared among many. Recognize that these are standard positions in the tradition.
The first claim is about the hyle's individuality; the second is about universals.
2
Grasp the definition of 'person'
Note the author's definition: 'person' (al-shakhs) is the quiddity restricted by individuation. Understand that the hyle in relation to form is analogous to this definition.
This definition is crucial to seeing the tension.
3
See the hint at resolution
The author ends by suggesting that the difficulty can be resolved if the statements about the hyle are interpreted in a certain way, which will be explained later. This sets up the next topic.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولك أن تقول : مراده أن كل موجود إذا لوحظ اتصافه بالوجود كان متعيناً، والهيولى إنما توجد مع مقارنة الصورة، والحق أن الجمع بين القول باتحاد هيولى العناصر شخصاً وامتناع وجود الكلي الطبيعي في الخارج، واشتراكه بين كثيرين محل تأمل، سيما إذا كان الشخص عبارة عن الماهية المقيدة بالتشخص كالهيولى بالنسبة إلى الصورة إلا أن يؤول كلامهم في الهيولى بما سنذكره في المقصد الثاني عشر.
And you may say: He meant that every existent, when observed as described with existence, is determined, and the hyle only exists with the accompaniment of the form. And the truth is that combining the statement that the hyle of the elements is one in person with the impossibility of the existence of the natural universal in the external and its sharing among many is a matter for reflection, especially since the person (al-shakhs) is the quiddity restricted by individuation, like the hyle in relation to the form, unless their statement about the hyle is interpreted according to what we will mention in the twelfth topic.
Source pages p. 91

Commentary
This passage presents a critical reflection. It first notes that every existent, when considered with existence, is determined, and the hyle only exists with a form. Then it questions the consistency of two positions: (1) that the hyle of the elements is one in person, and (2) that the natural universal cannot exist externally and be shared among many. This combination is problematic, especially since 'person' (al-shakhs) is defined as the quiddity restricted by individuation (ta'shakhkhush), and the hyle in relation to form is analogous. However, the author hints that this difficulty may be resolved by interpreting the statements about the hyle in a certain way, which will be discussed in the next topic.

The dispute over universals is merely verbal
Argues that the dispute about universals is merely verbal after clarifying ontological fact.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the dispute about the existence of universal natures is merely verbal, because only individuals exist externally and universals are abstracted by the mind.

Core Idea
The dispute about universals is just a confusion about words.

After discussing the attributes of existence, the text now addresses a fundamental question: do universal natures (like 'humanity') exist in the external world? Some affirm, others deny. This passage clarifies that the disagreement is only verbal once we realize that external existence belongs solely to individuals, and universals are mental abstractions. The passage then considers and refutes a potential objection.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the literal translation. Notice the flow: a decisive claim, an objection, then a rebuttal.
Pay attention to the technical terms: أشخاص, طبائع كلية, انتزاع, تشخص.
2
Identify the two main parts
The passage has a thesis ('no dispute except in expression') and an objection with answer. Mark where the objection begins ('وأما ما يقال...').
3
Understand why the answer resolves the dispute
The objection claims that a universal nature like humanity exists externally as multiplied. The answer shows that each individual includes an additional element (individuation), so none is the bare nature. This preserves the claim that only individuals exist externally.
The key term is تشخص (individuation) – the property that makes each individual distinct.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وجود في الخارج إلا للأشخاص، والطبائع الكلية منتزعة منها، فلا نزاع إلا في العبارة. وأما ما يقال : من أن الطبيعة الإنسانية مثلاً قابلة في نفسها للتعدد والتكثر، فتحتاج إلى من يكثرها، فإذا تكثرت بتكثير الفاعل ووجدت تلك الكثرة في الخارج، كان كل واحد منها عين تلك الطبيعة، فتكون الطبيعة الإنسانية موجودة في الخارج على أنها متكثرة، لا على أنها متصفة بالوحدة حتى يلزم ذلك المحذور فجوابه : أن كل واحد تلك الكثرة لا بد أن يشتمل على أمر زائد هو تشخصه ،وتعينه، فليس شيء منها تلك الطبيعة . كيف ولو كان كذلك لكان كل واحد من تلك الكثرة عين منها، وهو باطل بديهة.
Existence in the external is only for individuals, and the universal natures are abstracted from them, so there is no dispute except in expression. As for what is said: that human nature, for example, is in itself receptive to multiplicity and plurality, so it needs someone to multiply it; when it is multiplied by the multiplier's action and that multiplicity occurs in the external, each one of them is that nature itself, so human nature exists in the external as multiplied, not as described with unity such that that problem follows; its answer is that each one of that multiplicity must include an additional thing which is its individuation and determination, so none of them is that nature. How so? For if it were so, then each one of that multiplicity would be identical to the other, which is intuitively false.
Source pages p. 92

Commentary
This passage first states that there is no real dispute: external existence belongs only to individuals, and universal natures are abstracted from them by the mind. The dispute is merely verbal—those who deny the existence of universals mean existence by themselves, while those who affirm them mean existence through abstraction. Then it presents an objection: human nature is receptive to multiplicity in itself, and when the agent multiplies it, each individual becomes that nature itself, so the nature exists externally as multiplied without the problem of one thing being in many places. The answer is that each individual includes an additional element, its individuation (tashakhkhush) and determination (ta'ayyun), so none of them is the bare nature. If they were, then each individual would be identical to the other, which is absurd.

Key Terms
أشخاص
طبائع كلية
انتزاع
تعدد
تشخص
عينية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The dispute about universals is a substantive ontological disagreement about whether universals exist externally as entities distinct from individuals.
Correction: The passage clarifies that the dispute is merely verbal: both sides agree that only individuals exist externally; universals are abstractions. Those who affirm universals mean they exist as mental concepts, not as extra-mental realities.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is the dispute about the existence of universal natures merely verbal?
A) Because both parties agree that universals exist in the mind.
B) Because existence in the external is only for individuals, and universals are abstracted from them.
C) Because the dispute is about words, not concepts.
D) Because the issue is too subtle for real disagreement.

Key Takeaway
The dispute about universals is merely verbal because only individuals exist externally; universals are mental abstractions from them.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you think about concepts like 'justice' or 'humanity', do you unconsciously treat them as real things that exist somewhere? How might that verbal confusion affect your actions toward real individuals?
?
The passage says that each person has an individuation that makes them unique and not identical to a universal nature. Do you truly see every person you meet as this irreplaceable individual, or do you reduce them to a category?
?
If the dispute about universals is merely verbal, are there other disagreements in your life that are really just about words? Can you identify one such disagreement and commit to resolving it by clarifying terms?

Imam al-Razi's Proof: Determination is an Existent Attribute
Imam al-Razi's reductio proof that determination is existent.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Imam al-Razi's reductio argument that determination (ta'ayyun) cannot be non-existential and therefore must be an existent attribute.

Core Idea
Determination cannot be non-existence because non-existence lacks distinction and would eliminate the thing itself.

Imam al-Razi presents a concise proof that determination (ta'ayyun) is an existent attribute, not a privation. He uses a reductio argument to show that if determination were non-existential, it would lead to absurd consequences. This lesson walks through his argument step by step, clarifying the key terms and logical structure.

Guided Path
1
Understand the claim and key terms
Imam al-Razi is arguing that determination (ta'ayyun) is an existent thing (amr wujudi). First, identify the key terms: ta'ayyun (determination), adami (non-existential), adam mutlaq (absolute non-existence).
2
Follow the reductio argument
The argument has two parts. First, if determination were non-existential, it would have to be absolute non-existence, but that is false because absolute non-existence has no distinction. Second, if determination were non-existence, then the determined thing would be absolutely non-existent, which is absurd.
Notice the logical structure: if P then Q, Q is false, so not P.
3
Reflect on the conclusion
Since both consequences are impossible, determination must be existent. Consider why this matters for understanding attributes in kalam.
This argument is foundational for discussions about quiddity and existence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد احتج الإمام الرازي) على كون التعين أمراً وجودياً بأنه لو كان عدمياً لكان إما عدماً مطلقاً، وأنه ظاهر البطلان )؛ لأن العدم المطلق لا تميز فيه وأيضاً لو كان التعين عدماً لكان المتعين معدوماً مطلقاً؛ لأن المتصف بالعدم المطلق معدوم مطلق مع ظهور بطلانه .
Imam al-Razi argued that determination is an existent thing because if it were non-existential, it would be either absolute non-existence, and that is clearly false; because absolute non-existence has no distinction in it. Also, if determination were non-existence, then the determined thing would be absolutely non-existent; because the thing described with absolute non-existence is absolutely non-existent, and this is clearly false.
Source pages p. 92

Commentary
This passage presents Imam al-Razi's proof that determination (ta'ayyun) is an existent attribute (amr wujudi). He argues by reductio: if determination were non-existential (adami), then it would have to be either absolute non-existence (adam mutlaq) or something else. If it were absolute non-existence, that is clearly false because absolute non-existence lacks any distinction (tamyiz). Moreover, if determination were non-existence, then the thing that is determined would be absolutely non-existent, which is absurd. Therefore, determination must be existent.

Key Terms
التعين
أمر وجودي
عدمي
العدم المطلق
تميز

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Assuming that determination is a privation or absence rather than a positive attribute.
Correction: Imam al-Razi proves that if determination were a privation (non-existence), it would result in absolute non-existence lacking distinction or rendering the thing non-existent, which is impossible. Therefore, determination must be an existent attribute.

Checkpoint
What is the main reason Imam al-Razi gives for determination being existent rather than non-existent?
A) Because non-existence cannot be predicated of anything.
B) Because if determination were non-existent, it would be absolute non-existence, which lacks distinction and would make the determined thing absolutely non-existent.
C) Because all attributes are existent.
D) Because determination is a property of quiddity, which is existent.

Key Takeaway
Determination (ta'ayyun) must be an existent attribute because it cannot be non-existential without leading to absurdity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If your own determination—what makes you uniquely you—were merely a lack or absence, you would be nothing at all. Do you live as if your identity is a real, positive gift from Allah, or do you reduce it to what you are not? What would change if you fully embraced your determination as an existent attribute that Allah has given you?
?
Al-Razi argues that non-existence cannot ground distinction. In your daily life, do you define yourself more by what you lack or by what you are? How does this lesson challenge you to see your own existence and the existence of others as genuinely real and valuable?

Proof that Determination is Existential
The commentator proves that determination (ta'ayyun) cannot be nonexistential (adami).

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why determination (ta'ayyun) must be an existential (wujudi) attribute rather than a nonexistential (adami) one, based on the logical argument from infinite regress.

Core Idea
Determination cannot be non-existence; assuming so leads to infinite regress.

The commentator presents a subtle logical argument proving that determination (ta'ayyun) is an existential attribute, not a mere negation. This is crucial for understanding the nature of entities in kalam. The argument uses the concept of lack-of-determination (la-ta'ayyun) and shows that assuming determination is nonexistential leads to an infinite regress or contradiction.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once through, following the translation. Notice how the commentator unpacks each part of the base text's statement.
2
Identify the two possibilities
The passage considers two possibilities for determination if it were a non-existence: either it is the non-existence of lack-of-determination (la-ta'ayyun) or the non-existence of another determination. Trace these in the text.
3
Understand the first branch: infinite regress
If determination were the non-existence of lack-of-determination, then lack-of-determination itself implies a determination (since it is defined as the absence of determination). This leads to an infinite chain of non-existences, which is impossible, so that determination must be existential.
4
Understand the second branch: similar reasoning
If determination were the non-existence of another determination, that other determination would also be a non-existence of something, again leading to an infinite regress or contradiction. Thus, it too must be existential.
5
Reflect on the conclusion
Notice how the argument uses the principle that attributing a quality that has existence in the external world requires the existence of that quality. This seals the case that determination is existential.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وإما عدماً مضافاً ) أي إلى شيء مخصوص، ولا شك أنه يكون عدماً لشيء ينافيه وهو إما اللاتعين الذي هو نقيض ذلك التعين المخصوص، أو التعين الاخر إذ ما سواهما من المفهومات يمكن اجتماعه منه فإن اللاتعين المطلق يصدق على كل تعين مخصوص ضرورة سلب تعين آخر عنه وكل مفهوم ما سوى التعين يمكن عروض التعين له . اللاتعين قوله: (فيكون هو وجودياً) أي يكون التعين الذي هو عدم اللاتعين وجودياً لأن التعين الذي اعتبر في مفهوم اللاتعين وجودي؛ لأنه لو كان عدمياً لكان عدماً للاتعين؛ لأنه المفروض، وهذا اللاتعين أيضاً مشتمل على التعين الذي هو عدم اللاتعين، وهكذا فيلزم اشتمال اللاتعين الذي فرض التعين عدما له على أعدام غير متناهية فلا يكون التعين الذي اعتبر في عدمياً، وإذا كان هذا التعين وجودياً كان التعين الذي فرض أنه عدم اللاتعين وجودياً؛ لأنه عينه لما عرفت من أنه لو لم يكن عينه لم يكن اللاتعين منافياً له . قوله : ( فذلك التعين الآخر إن كان عدماً تقدير الكلام فذلك التعين الآخر إن كان عدمياً كان عدماً لشيء. قوله فهو (وجود) فيكون وجودياً بناء على مساواة الوجود الوجودي لمساواة العدمي بالعدم . قوله : ( والتعين الآخر مثله أي في كونه تعيناً سواء كان ذاتياً لهما أو عرضياً . قوله: (فيكون هو أيضاً وجودياً) بناء على ما تقرر من أن اتصاف شيء بصفة من شأنها الوجود في الخارج فرع وجود الصفة، وإلا لجاز اتصاف الجسم بالحركة المعدومة وهو سفسطة
His saying: 'or a non-existence that is added' i.e., to something specific, and there is no doubt that it is a non-existence of something that contradicts it, and it is either the lack-of-determination (la-ta'ayyun) which is the opposite of that specific determination (ta'ayyun), or the other determination, since other than these two concepts can be combined with it. For absolute lack-of-determination applies to every specific determination necessarily because another determination is negated from it, and every concept other than determination can have determination occur to it. Lack-of-determination. His saying: 'so it would be existential (wujudi)' i.e., the determination that is the non-existence of lack-of-determination is existential because the determination that is considered in the concept of lack-of-determination is existential; for if it were nonexistential (adami), it would be a non-existence of lack-of-determination because that is assumed, and this lack-of-determination also includes the determination that is the non-existence of lack-of-determination, and so on, thus necessitating that the lack-of-determination which is assumed to have determination as its non-existence include infinite non-existences, so the determination considered in [lack-of-determination] is not nonexistential. And when this determination is existential, then the determination that is assumed to be the non-existence of lack-of-determination is existential because it is the same as it, as you know that if it were not the same, then lack-of-determination would not contradict it. His saying: 'then that other determination if it is non-existence' the implied phrase is: then that other determination if it is nonexistential, it is a non-existence of something. His saying: 'so it is existence' so it is existential based on the equality of existential existence to the equality of nonexistential with non-existence. His saying: 'and the other determination is like it' i.e., in being a determination, whether it is essential to both or accidental. His saying: 'so it also is existential' based on what has been established that the attribution of something to a quality whose nature is existence in the external world is a branch of the existence of the quality, otherwise it would be permissible to attribute a body with a non-existent motion, which is sophistry.
Source pages p. 93

Commentary
This passage is a proof that determination (ta'ayyun) must be existential (wujudi). The commentator explains the meaning of a statement from the base text. The argument begins by considering the possibility that determination is a non-existence that is added (i.e., relative). It must be a non-existence of something that contradicts it, which is either the lack-of-determination (la-ta'ayyun) or another determination. First, if it is the non-existence of lack-of-determination, then lack-of-determination itself includes a determination (since it is defined as the negation of determination), leading to an infinite regress of non-existences unless that determination is existential. Second, if it is the non-existence of another determination, that other determination, being nonexistential, would also be a non-existence of something, and by similar reasoning must be existential. The commentator then explains each sub-statement, concluding that determination cannot be nonexistential without contradiction.

Key Terms
تعين
لا تعين
عدم
وجود
عدمي
وجودي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that 'adami' simply means 'adam' (absolute non-existence) without distinction.
Correction: The passage carefully distinguishes between 'adami' (nonexistential) and 'adam' (non-existence). Determination being nonexistential means it is a non-existence of something specific, not pure nothingness.

Checkpoint
According to the proof, what would happen if determination (ta'ayyun) were nonexistential (adami)?
A) It would be impossible for anything to have determination.
B) It would lead to an infinite regress or contradiction.
C) It would make determination identical to existence.
D) It would cause all things to be indeterminate.

Key Takeaway
Determination (ta'ayyun) must be existential because assuming it is nonexistential leads to an infinite regress or contradiction.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The argument shows that defining yourself by what you are not leads to an infinite regress of negations. Do you identify more by what you are not (e.g., not a sinner, not like others) than by the positive reality of who you are in Allah's sight? What would change today if you grounded your identity in the existential gift of being a believer?
?
If our very determination (distinctness) is a positive existential attribute from Allah, not a mere absence of others, how should that affect your gratitude for your unique existence? Take a moment to thank Allah for making you specifically you, and commit to seeing yourself as a positive creation, not just a negation of faults.
?
The proof warns that assuming determination as nonexistential leads to absurdity. Are there areas in your life where you treat your good deeds or character as mere negations (e.g., 'I am not a liar') rather than positive, existential realities? How can you affirm and strengthen those positive traits as real existences?

The Objection Answered: Determination is Not Necessarily Non-existence
The commentator addresses the objection that determination being nonexistential leads to a contradiction, and gives the initial response.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the objection that determination could be nonexistential is refuted by clarifying the meaning of 'adami.

Core Idea
'Adami does not mean non-existence; it is a relative predicate.

In this passage, the commentator addresses a key objection to the proof that determination (ta'ayyun) is existential. The objector argues that if determination were nonexistential, it would lead to a contradiction, but the commentator shows that the term 'adami does not imply non-existence in the same way. Instead, 'adami is contrasted with 'wujudi' as a relative notion.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection
Carefully read the objector's argument that if determination is 'adami, then it would be non-existence, leading to a contradiction.
Notice the objector uses the terms 'adami and wujudi.
2
Identify the core claim
The objector claims that if determination is nonexistential, it must be non-existence, but the commentator denies this implication.
The key is the meaning of 'adami.
3
Examine the response
The commentator responds that 'adami is opposed to 'wujudi, but that does not mean it is non-existence. He explains the intended meaning of 'wujudi in this context.
The response relies on the distinction between concept and referent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واعلم أن تقرير الاحتجاج المذكور على ما حررناه يدفع جميع الشكوك التي أوردها الناظرون في قوله : ( فيكون هو وجودياً فيه منع سنده قضية الامتناع واللا امتناع. قوله : ( وإما أن يكون عدماً لتعين (آخر إن أريد بالتعين واللاتعين مفهوماهما فلا حصر؛ لجواز أن يكون التعين عدماً لمفهوم ،آخر وإن أريد ما صدقا عليه فلا نسلم أن ما صدق عليه اللاتعين فهو عدمي، فيكون نقيضه ثبوتياً . كيف واللاتعين صادق على ما سوى التعين من الحقائق ؟ . قوله : (فهذا) عدم العدم فهو (وجود فيه أن مفهوم العدم غير الوجود وكذا ما صدق هو عليه. وأيضاً إن كان المراد بالوجود والعدم في قوله إن كان عدماً وإن كان وجوداً مفهوم العدم والوجود، فالحصر ممنوع وسيورده المصنف على أصل الملازمة أيضاً. وإن كان المراد ما صدق فهذا أيضاً (وجود). فثبت أن كون التعين عدمياً يستلزم كونه وجودياً. هذا خلف فيكون وجودياً . ( والجواب : لا نسلم أنه لو كان ( التعين ( عدمياً لكان عدماً)، وإنما يلزم ذلك إذا كان العدمي بمعنى العدم أو مستلزماً له، وهو ممنوع؛ لأن العدمي يقابل الوجودي، كما أن العدم يقابل الوجود، فلو كان العدمي عدماً لكان الوجودي وجوداً، وليس كذلك بل المراد بالوجودي ما يكون ثبوته لموصوفه بوجوده له أي الوجودي هذا المقام، سوى ما ذكره المصنف من منع الملازمة من أن العدمي لا يلزم أن يكون عدماً كما لا يخفى على من تأمل وأجاد . قوله : (بمعنى العدم وعلى هذا التقدير تكون الملازمة بينهما بحسب التغاير الاعتباري. قوله : ( أو مستلزماً له) بحيث يصدق عليه. قوله : ( لكان الوجودي وجوداً إذ لو كان غيره لم يصدق الوجود عليه، فيصدق العدم عليه مع عدم صدق العدمي عليه لصدق الوجودي عليه قوله : ( بل المراد إلخ) تقدير الكلام بل أعم منه لأن المراد بالوجودي إلخ . قوله : ( ما يكون ثبوته لموصوفه بوجوده (له) إن كان وجود العرض في نفسه هو وجوده في الموصوف، كما اختاره المحقق التفتازاني وصرح به الشيخ الرئيس فثبوت شيء لشيء أعم من عليه نفس الوجود والعدم فكذلك، وإن كان ما صدق عليه الوجود والعدم بالاشتقاق فنختار أن ذلك التعين معدوم، ولا يلزم أن يكون هذا التعين وجوداً؛ لأن عدم المعدوم ليس بوجود ولا موجود كما أشرنا إليه . مع جواز قوله : ( والتعين الآخر مثله إن أراد بالمثلية المشاركة في التعينية فلا يتوهم من وجودية أحد المثلين بهذا المعنى وجودية الآخر، وإن أراد الاتفاق في الماهية فلا نسلم المثلية، لم لا يجوز أن تكون التعينات متخلفة في الماهية متشاركة في عارض هو مفهوم التعين، وعلى تقدير تسليمها لا يلزم من وجود أحد المتماثلات وجود جميعها، فإن زيداً وعمراً مثلان اتصاف أحدهما بالوجود والآخر بالعدم قوله : ( أو مستلزماً له بحيث يحمل عليه مواطأة، وإلا فلزوم ذلك ممنوع حينئذ. قوله : ( لكان الوجودي وجوداً) قد يمنع ذلك لجواز أن يتصف المتقابلان بشيء واحد، كالامتناع واللا امتناع المتصفين بالعدم وجوابه : أن ليس المراد بقوله : فلو كان العدمي عدماً أنه لو كان متصفاً بالعدم، بل أنه لو كان بمعنى العدم أو مستلزماً لحمله عليه مواطأة، فمنع الملازمة على هذا مكابرة، فتأمل. قوله : (بل المراد بالوجودي إلخ) فسره ليعلم مقابله الذي هو المقصود بالبيان أصالة، أعني العدمي، والمراد أن الوجودي من الصفات ما ذكره بقرينة قوله : الموصوفه، والتخصيص بناء على أن الكلام في وجودية التعين الذي هو من الأمور الغير المستقلة
And know that the exposition of the aforementioned proof according to what we have written repels all the doubts that the investigators have raised in his saying: 'so it is existential' – there is a denial of it, its basis being the issue of impossibility and non-impossibility. His saying: 'or that it is a non-existence of another determination' – if by determination and lack-of-determination their concepts are meant, then there is no exclusive enumeration; because it is possible that determination is a non-existence of another concept. And if what is meant is their referents, then we do not grant that the referent of lack-of-determination is nonexistential, so its opposite would be positive. How can it be, when lack-of-determination applies to realities other than determination? His saying: 'so this is non-existence of non-existence, so it is existence' – in it, the concept of non-existence is other than existence, and likewise its referent. Also, if what is meant by existence and non-existence in his saying 'if it were non-existence' and 'if it were existence' is the concept of non-existence and existence, then the exclusive enumeration is denied, and the author will also bring it up concerning the principle of the implication. And if what is meant is the referent, then this too is existence. So it is established that determination being nonexistential necessitates it being existential. This is a contradiction, so it is existential. (The answer: We do not grant that if determination were nonexistential it would be a non-existence; this follows only if 'nonexistential' is in the sense of non-existence or implies it, and this is denied; because 'nonexistential' is contrasted with 'existential', just as non-existence is contrasted with existence. For if the nonexistential were non-existence, then the existential would be existence, but it is not so. Rather, by 'existential' is meant what has subsistence for its subject by its existence, i.e., the existential in this context – apart from what the author mentioned in denying the implication that the nonexistential does not have to be non-existence, as is not hidden from one who reflects and does well. His saying: 'in the sense of non-existence' – and on this assumption, the implication between them is according to notional difference. His saying: 'or implies it' such that it applies to it. His saying: 'then the existential would be existence' – for if it were otherwise, existence would not apply to it, so non-existence would apply to it while the nonexistential does not apply to it due to the existential applying to it. His saying: 'rather, the meaning is etc.' – the implied phrase is: rather it is more general than that, because by 'existential' etc. His saying: 'what has subsistence for its subject by its existence' – if the existence of the accident in itself is its existence in the subject, as chosen by al-Muhaqqiq al-Taftazani and stated by the Chief (Ibn Sina), then the subsistence of something for something is more general than existence and non-existence themselves, so it is likewise. And if what is meant is what existence and non-existence apply to by derivation, then we choose that that determination is non-existent, and it does not necessitate that this determination is existence; because the non-existence of the non-existent is not existence nor existent, as we have indicated. Along with the permissibility of his saying: 'and the other determination is like it' – if he means by similarity sharing in determination-ness, then one should not imagine from the existentiality of one of the two similars in this sense the existentiality of the other. And if he means agreement in quiddity, then we do not grant the similarity; why is it not permissible that determinations differ in quiddity while sharing in an accident which is the concept of determination? And on the assumption of granting it, the existence of one of the similars does not necessitate the existence of all of them; for Zayd and 'Amr are two similars, one of them being described with existence and the other with non-existence. His saying: 'or implies it such that it applies to it by way of agreement' – otherwise, the necessity of that is denied at that time. His saying: 'then the existential would be existence' – one may deny that because it is possible for two opposites to be described with one thing, like impossibility and non-impossibility being described with non-existence. And its answer: that what is meant by his saying 'if the nonexistential were non-existence' is not that it is described with non-existence, but that it is in the sense of non-existence or implies its application to it by way of agreement, so denying the implication on this is obstinacy, so reflect. His saying: 'rather, the meaning is etc.' – he interpreted it so that its counterpart which is the primary object of explanation is known, namely the nonexistential. And the meaning is that the existential is among the attributes what he mentioned, by the indication of his saying: 'its subject' – and the specification is based on the fact that the discussion is about the existentiality of determination, which is among non-independent matters.
Source pages p. 93

Commentary
This passage is an objection and response sequence defending the proof that determination is existential. The commentator first notes that his exposition repels doubts. The objection challenges the claim that if determination is nonexistential it leads to contradiction. The objector argues that the term 'nonexistential' (adami) may not imply non-existence (adam) in the same way; it could be a relative notion. The response clarifies that 'adami is opposed to 'wujudi' (existential), and what is meant by 'wujudi' is what subsists by its existence in a subject. The explanation distinguishes between the sense of 'adami as 'adam itself or what implies it. Further objections about similarity (mithliyya) between determinations are addressed: similarity in being determinations does not entail existentiality of all, and even if they are similar in quiddity, the existence of one does not necessitate existence of another. The passage concludes by defining 'wujudi' as an attribute that is dependent on a subject, since the discussion concerns the existentiality of determination which is not an independent entity.

Key Terms
عدمي (adami)
وجودي (wujudi)
عدم (adam)
وجود (wujud)
تعين (ta'ayyun)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The term 'adami always means non-existence (adam).
Correction: In this context, 'adami is opposed to 'wujudi and does not necessarily imply non-existence; it is a relative predicate.

Checkpoint
What is the objector's main argument?
A) Determination is clearly existential.
B) If determination is nonexistential, it must be non-existence, leading to a contradiction.
C) The terms are unclear.
D) The proof is invalid.

Key Takeaway
The key move in the response is to deny that 'adami (nonexistential) is equivalent to 'adam (non-existence); instead, 'adami is a relative term contrasted with 'wujudi.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever mistaken a relative description (like 'adami) for an absolute judgment (like 'adam), leading to a misunderstanding in your own beliefs? How will you guard against that kind of conflation in your study of theology?
?
This lesson reveals that precision in definitions can save one from contradictions. Where in your own understanding of Islamic theology might you be unwittingly confusing terms? What step will you take this week to clarify one such term?
?
The commentator says the response is 'not hidden from one who reflects and does well.' When was the last time you truly reflected on a theological concept until you grasped its nuance? Will you commit to deeper reflection on the next difficult topic you encounter?

Understanding 'Adami and 'Wujudi: The Full Clarification
The commentator provides a precise definition of 'wujudi, addresses the similarity objection, and concludes the discussion.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the precise meanings of 'adami and 'wujudi in kalam discourse, and how the issue of similarity between determinations is resolved.

Core Idea
'Wujudi means an attribute that subsists through its existence in a subject; similarity does not entail shared existentiality.

This passage extends the response by clarifying the definitions of 'existential' and 'nonexistential' and addressing an additional objection about similar determinations. The commentator explains that 'wujudi in this context refers to attributes that are not independent but subsist in a subject. He then addresses the worry that if two determinations are similar, the existentiality of one would imply the existentiality of the other, showing why this does not follow.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition
Focus on the commentator's definition of 'wujudi': 'what has subsistence for its subject by its existence'. Understand how this applies to determination.
This definition is key to the entire argument.
2
Analyze the similarity objection
The objector raises the issue of two similar determinations: if one is existential, does the other have to be? The commentator explains that similarity in being determinations does not require agreement in quiddity or existentiality.
The example of Zayd and 'Amr illustrates this.
3
Confirm the definitions
Review how the commentator distinguishes between the concept of 'adami and its referent, and why this resolves the initial objection.

Source Text

( والجواب : لا نسلم أنه لو كان ( التعين ( عدمياً لكان عدماً)، وإنما يلزم ذلك إذا كان العدمي بمعنى العدم أو مستلزماً له، وهو ممنوع؛ لأن العدمي يقابل الوجودي، كما أن العدم يقابل الوجود، فلو كان العدمي تأمل وأجاد . قوله : (بمعنى العدم وعلى هذا التقدير تكون الملازمة بينهما بحسب التغاير الاعتباري. قوله : ( أو مستلزماً له) بحيث يصدق عليه. قوله : ( لكان الوجودي وجوداً إذ لو كان غيره لم يصدق الوجود عليه، فيصدق العدم عليه مع عدم صدق العدمي عليه لصدق الوجودي عليه قوله : ( بل المراد إلخ) تقدير الكلام بل أعم منه لأن المراد بالوجودي إلخ . قوله : ( ما يكون ثبوته لموصوفه بوجوده (له) إن كان وجود العرض في نفسه هو وجوده في الموصوف، كما اختاره المحقق التفتازاني وصرح به الشيخ الرئيس فثبوت شيء لشيء أعم من عليه نفس الوجود والعدم فكذلك، وإن كان ما صدق عليه الوجود والعدم بالاشتقاق فنختار أن ذلك التعين معدوم، ولا يلزم أن يكون هذا التعين وجوداً؛ لأن عدم المعدوم ليس بوجود ولا موجود كما أشرنا إليه . مع جواز قوله : ( والتعين الآخر مثله إن أراد بالمثلية المشاركة في التعينية فلا يتوهم من وجودية أحد المثلين بهذا المعنى وجودية الآخر، وإن أراد الاتفاق في الماهية فلا نسلم المثلية، لم لا يجوز أن تكون التعينات متخلفة في الماهية متشاركة في عارض هو مفهوم التعين، وعلى تقدير تسليمها لا يلزم من وجود أحد المتماثلات وجود جميعها، فإن زيداً وعمراً مثلان اتصاف أحدهما بالوجود والآخر بالعدم قوله : ( أو مستلزماً له بحيث يحمل عليه مواطأة، وإلا فلزوم ذلك ممنوع حينئذ. قوله : ( لكان الوجودي وجوداً) قد يمنع ذلك لجواز أن يتصف المتقابلان بشيء واحد، كالامتناع واللا امتناع المتصفين بالعدم وجوابه : أن ليس المراد بقوله : فلو كان العدمي عدماً أنه لو كان متصفاً بالعدم، بل أنه لو كان بمعنى العدم أو مستلزماً لحمله عليه مواطأة، فمنع الملازمة على هذا مكابرة، فتأمل. قوله : (بل المراد بالوجودي إلخ) فسره ليعلم مقابله الذي هو المقصود بالبيان أصالة، أعني العدمي، والمراد أن الوجودي من الصفات ما ذكره بقرينة قوله : الموصوفه، والتخصيص بناء على أن الكلام في وجودية التعين الذي هو من الأمور الغير المستقلة
And know that the exposition of the aforementioned proof according to what we have written repels all the doubts that the investigators have raised in his saying: 'so it is existential' – there is a denial of it, its basis being the issue of impossibility and non-impossibility. His saying: 'or that it is a non-existence of another determination' – if by determination and lack-of-determination their concepts are meant, then there is no exclusive enumeration; because it is possible that determination is a non-existence of another concept. And if what is meant is their referents, then we do not grant that the referent of lack-of-determination is nonexistential, so its opposite would be positive. How can it be, when lack-of-determination applies to realities other than determination? His saying: 'so this is non-existence of non-existence, so it is existence' – in it, the concept of non-existence is other than existence, and likewise its referent. Also, if what is meant by existence and non-existence in his saying 'if it were non-existence' and 'if it were existence' is the concept of non-existence and existence, then the exclusive enumeration is denied, and the author will also bring it up concerning the principle of the implication. And if what is meant is the referent, then this too is existence. So it is established that determination being nonexistential necessitates it being existential. This is a contradiction, so it is existential. (The answer: We do not grant that if determination were nonexistential it would be a non-existence; this follows only if 'nonexistential' is in the sense of non-existence or implies it, and this is denied; because 'nonexistential' is contrasted with 'existential', just as non-existence is contrasted with existence. For if the nonexistential were non-existence, then the existential would be existence, but it is not so. Rather, by 'existential' is meant what has subsistence for its subject by its existence, i.e., the existential in this context – apart from what the author mentioned in denying the implication that the nonexistential does not have to be non-existence, as is not hidden from one who reflects and does well. His saying: 'in the sense of non-existence' – and on this assumption, the implication between them is according to notional difference. His saying: 'or implies it' such that it applies to it. His saying: 'then the existential would be existence' – for if it were otherwise, existence would not apply to it, so non-existence would apply to it while the nonexistential does not apply to it due to the existential applying to it. His saying: 'rather, the meaning is etc.' – the implied phrase is: rather it is more general than that, because by 'existential' etc. His saying: 'what has subsistence for its subject by its existence' – if the existence of the accident in itself is its existence in the subject, as chosen by al-Muhaqqiq al-Taftazani and stated by the Chief (Ibn Sina), then the subsistence of something for something is more general than existence and non-existence themselves, so it is likewise. And if what is meant is what existence and non-existence apply to by derivation, then we choose that that determination is non-existent, and it does not necessitate that this determination is existence; because the non-existence of the non-existent is not existence nor existent, as we have indicated. Along with the permissibility of his saying: 'and the other determination is like it' – if he means by similarity sharing in determination-ness, then one should not imagine from the existentiality of one of the two similars in this sense the existentiality of the other. And if he means agreement in quiddity, then we do not grant the similarity; why is it not permissible that determinations differ in quiddity while sharing in an accident which is the concept of determination? And on the assumption of granting it, the existence of one of the similars does not necessitate the existence of all of them; for Zayd and 'Amr are two similars, one of them being described with existence and the other with non-existence. His saying: 'or implies it such that it applies to it by way of agreement' – otherwise, the necessity of that is denied at that time. His saying: 'then the existential would be existence' – one may deny that because it is possible for two opposites to be described with one thing, like impossibility and non-impossibility being described with non-existence. And its answer: that what is meant by his saying 'if the nonexistential were non-existence' is not that it is described with non-existence, but that it is in the sense of non-existence or implies its application to it by way of agreement, so denying the implication on this is obstinacy, so reflect. His saying: 'rather, the meaning is etc.' – he interpreted it so that its counterpart which is the primary object of explanation is known, namely the nonexistential. And the meaning is that the existential is among the attributes what he mentioned, by the indication of his saying: 'its subject' – and the specification is based on the fact that the discussion is about the existentiality of determination, which is among non-independent matters.
Source pages p. 93

Commentary
This passage is an objection and response sequence defending the proof that determination is existential. The commentator first notes that his exposition repels doubts. The objection challenges the claim that if determination is nonexistential it leads to contradiction. The objector argues that the term 'nonexistential' (adami) may not imply non-existence (adam) in the same way; it could be a relative notion. The response clarifies that 'adami is opposed to 'wujudi' (existential), and what is meant by 'wujudi' is what subsists by its existence in a subject. The explanation distinguishes between the sense of 'adami as 'adam itself or what implies it. Further objections about similarity (mithliyya) between determinations are addressed: similarity in being determinations does not entail existentiality of all, and even if they are similar in quiddity, the existence of one does not necessitate existence of another. The passage concludes by defining 'wujudi' as an attribute that is dependent on a subject, since the discussion concerns the existentiality of determination which is not an independent entity.

Key Terms
عدمي (adami)
وجودي (wujudi)
ماهية (mahiyya)
لاثنين (mithliyya)
تعين (ta'ayyun)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: If two things are similar (mithlayn), they must share all properties including existentiality.
Correction: Similarity does not require sharing existentiality; Zayd and 'Amr are similar but one may be existent and the other non-existent.

Checkpoint
According to the commentator, what does 'wujudi' mean in this context?
A) Something that exists in itself.
B) What has subsistence for its subject by its existence.
C) The opposite of non-existence.
D) A quality that is independent.

Key Takeaway
The precise definition of 'wujudi as a dependent attribute resolves the initial objection, and similarity between determinations does not entail shared existentiality.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The definition of existential attributes reminds us that some qualities depend entirely on their subject. What in your own character or faith do you treat as if it exists on its own, when in reality it depends on your constant connection to Allah? What is one step you can take today to reattach that dependency?

The Circularity Argument on Essence Portion Discrimination
Objection and answer on the dependence of discrimination of an essence portion on individuation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the circularity argument regarding the dependence of the discrimination of a portion of quiddity on individuation, and the proper resolution that avoids it.

Core Idea
Distinguishing portions of the same quiddity requires individuation, but careful analysis avoids circularity.

This passage presents a subtle objection in Islamic metaphysics: if a portion of quiddity can only be distinguished from another portion by individuation, and individuation itself requires prior distinction, then we face circularity. The author presents and refutes a common answer before offering the proper resolution. Let's examine the argument step by step.

Guided Path
1
Understand the objection
Read the first sentence of the passage which states the circularity problem. Ask yourself: why does discrimination of a portion depend on conjunction with individuation?
The objection assumes that without prior discrimination, individuation cannot preferentially attach to one portion.
2
Identify the initial answer and its flaw
The passage gives an initial answer: quiddity is distinguished by itself. But the author notes this misses the point—what matters is distinguishing portions of the same quiddity, not quiddity from others.
3
Grasp the proper resolution
The proper answer involves temporal simultaneity between conjunction and discrimination, and the conceptual nature of conjunction. Understand why this avoids circularity.
The key is that the conjunction is mental, not external.
4
Note the final rejection
The passage ends by rejecting the claim that the answer works if individuation is privative. This shows the depth of the discussion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تميزها وتميزها موقوف على انضمامه إليها فيدور وأجيب عنه: بأن الماهية ممتازة عن غيرها بذاتها لا بانضمام التعين إليها. وفيه نظر؛ إذ مرادهم امتياز حصة من الماهية عن حصة أخرى منها؛ إذ لولا امتياز إحداهما عن الأخرى لم يكن اختصاص التعين بإحداهما وانضمامه إليها أولى من العكس. وذلك أي امتياز الحصة عن الحصة إنما يكون بالتعين لا بذات الماهية، بل الجواب أن يقال: الانضمام مع الامتياز زماناً، وإن كان متقدماً عليه ذاتاً، ولا استحالة في ذلك، كما في اختصاص الفصول بحصص الأجناس وتوضيحه أن التعين أو الفصل ينضم انتزاعياً، فلا انضمام في الخارج حتى يتوقف على تميزها والانضمام في الذهن وإن توقف على تميزها وتصورها لكن تميزها الذهني لا يتوقف على انضمامه إليها، بل على انتزاعه منها. فما قيل: إنه جار على تقدير كونه عدمياً أيضاً وهم.
Its discrimination and its discrimination are dependent on its conjunction with it, so there is circularity. And it was answered: That quiddity is distinguished from other than itself by its essence, not by conjunction of individuation with it. But there is consideration in this answer; because what they mean is the distinction of a portion of quiddity from another portion of it; for if there were no distinction of one from the other, the specification of individuation with one of them and its conjunction with it would not be more appropriate than the opposite. And that, i.e., the distinction of the portion from the portion, is only by individuation, not by the quiddity's essence. Rather, the answer is to say: The conjunction [occurs] simultaneously with the distinction temporally, even if it is prior to it in essence, and there is no impossibility in that, as in the specification of differentiae with the portions of genera. And its clarification is that individuation or differentia is conjoined conceptually, so there is no external conjunction such that it is dependent on their distinction; and conjunction in the mind, even if it depends on their distinction and conception, their mental distinction does not depend on its conjunction with them, but on its abstraction from them. So what was said—that it holds on the assumption that it is also privative—is an illusion.
Source pages p. 97

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer sequence concerning the dependence of the discrimination of a portion of quiddity on individuation. The objector first argues that if the discrimination of a portion of quiddity is dependent on the conjunction of individuation with it, and individuation's conjunction with that portion is in turn dependent on prior discrimination (otherwise why that portion rather than another?), then circularity results. The answer given is that the quiddity is distinguished from others by itself, not by individuation. But the commentator notes that this misses the point: what is at stake is the distinction of one portion of the same quiddity from another portion, not the quiddity from something else. That intra-species distinction cannot be by the quiddity's essence alone because the essence is common; it requires individuation. So the proper answer is to say that the conjunction of individuation with a portion occurs simultaneously with discrimination, not before it, in a temporal sense, even if in essence the conjunction is prior. This avoids circularity because the conjunction is not external but mental (conceptual); in the mind, the discrimination of the portion does not depend on the conjunction of individuation but on its abstraction. The passage ends by rejecting the claim that this answer also works if individuation is privative, calling it an illusion.

Key Terms
تميز
الماهية
التعين
انضمام
حصة
انتزاع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that saying 'quiddity is distinguished by itself' solves the circularity problem.
Correction: That answer only works for distinguishing quiddity from other quiddities, not for distinguishing portions of the same quiddity, which is the actual issue.

Checkpoint
What is the main point of the objection in this passage?
A) Individuation must be external to avoid circularity.
B) The discrimination of a portion of quiddity cannot be prior to individuation without leading to circularity.
C) Quiddity is distinguished by itself.
D) The conjunction of individuation is simultaneous with discrimination.

Key Takeaway
The proper resolution to the circularity objection lies in recognizing that conjunction and distinction can be simultaneous temporally, and that individuation is a conceptual abstraction, not an external conjunction.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you mentally separate one person from another, do you assume the distinction is inherent in them or that you are adding a conceptual label? How does this lesson's claim that discrimination can be simultaneous with conjunction challenge your usual way of categorizing people?
?
Think of a belief you hold about your own identity that you thought was based on your essence alone. Can you identify an aspect of that identity that actually depends on a conceptual addition (like a label or role) which you might have assumed was intrinsic? How does this lesson's resolution of circularity help you see the relationship between your essence and those additions differently?
?
The passage resolves a logical circularity by appealing to temporal simultaneity and conceptual abstraction. Is there a tension in your life where you feel stuck between two dependencies (e.g., 'I need to change my habits to change my character, but I need to change my character to change my habits')? How might the lesson's insight—that two things can be interdependent yet not circular if viewed temporally—open a way forward for you?

Second Argument Against External Individuation: Infinite Regress and Its Critique
Argument, answer, critique, and counter-objection on external individuation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the second argument against external individuation, the proposed answer, the author's critique, and the initial counter-objection involving the Necessary Being.

Core Idea
If individuation is external, it needs another individuation, leading to an infinite regress.

This passage presents a key debate in Islamic philosophy: can individuation (ta‘ayyun) be an external entity? The second argument claims that if it were, it would itself require individuation, causing an infinite regress. An answer based on distinguishing essence versus accident is offered, but the author criticizes it by arguing that each individuation has a universal quiddity. The passage ends with an incomplete objection invoking the Necessary Being.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once to get the flow, then read the translation. Note the different voices: the objector, the answerer, the author (al-Jurjani), and a subsequent objector.
The passage ends abruptly; the last sentence is incomplete.
2
Identify the argument and its structure
The second argument is presented first. Identify the logical steps: if individuation is external → it needs another individuation → infinite regress. Then note the answer given: common concept of individuation is an accident, individuals are distinguished by their own essences.
The answer tries to avoid regress by saying no additional individuation is needed if essence itself distinguishes.
3
Understand the author's critique
The author (al-Jurjani / the commentator) critiques the answer: every individual of individuation has a universal quiddity (mahiyya kulliyya) in the mind, so distinguishing essence alone is not sufficient. This restores the regress argument.
The critique hinges on the idea that universality is inherent in any external existent.
4
Examine the counter-objection (incomplete)
A new objector denies that every individuation has a universal quiddity, citing the Necessary Being as an exception. The passage breaks off before the full objection is given.
Think about why the Necessary Being might be an exception: it has no universal quiddity in the sense of being shared.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الوجه الثاني: لو كان التعين موجوداً خارجياً لكان معيناً، فإن كل موجود خارجي لا بد أن يكون متعيناً في نفسه، فهو أي كل واحد من التعين مشارك للتعينات الأخر في كونها تعيناً ويمتاز عنها بتعين آخر يخصه فيتسلسل، إذ ننقل الكلام إلى ذلك التعين الآخر. وأجيب عنه: بأن كونه تعيناً أي مفهوم التعين المشترك بين التعينات أمر عارض للتعينات، وهي متمايزة بذواتها المخصوصة والمحوج إلى التمايز بتعين زائد هو الاشتراك في الماهية دون الاشتراك في العوارض. قال المصنف: وفيه نظر؛ لأن كل تعين أي كل فرد من أفراد التعين فله ماهية كلية في العقل ضرورة؛ لأن كل موجود في الخارج كذلك، سواء كان له ما يشاركه في نوعه أم لا بل انحصر نوعه في شخصه، وتعينه غير ماهيته؛ لأنه لا يقبل الشركة بخلاف ماهيته ويتم الدليل بلزوم التسلسل، ولقائل أن يقول: لا نسلم أن كل تعين له ماهية كلية ينتزعها العقل من هويته، ودعوى الضرورة هاهنا غير مسموعة كيف والقاعدة القائلة بأن كل موجود خارجي كذلك منقوض عندهم بالواجب تعالى، بل كل فرد من أفراد التعين هو في
The second aspect: If individuation were an external existent, it would be determinate, for every external existent must be determinate in itself; so each one of the individuations shares with the other individuations in being an individuation and is distinguished from them by another individuation specific to it, leading to infinite regress, for we transfer the discussion to that other individuation. And it was answered: That it is an individuation, i.e., the common concept of individuation among individuations, is an accident of the individuations, and they are distinguished by their particular essences, and what necessitates distinction by an additional individuation is commonality in quiddity, not commonality in accidents. The author said: But there is consideration in this; because every individuation, i.e., every individual of the individuals of individuation, has a universal quiddity in the mind necessarily, because every existent in the outside is likewise, whether or not it has something sharing its type, even if its type is confined to its individual; and its individuation is other than its quiddity because it does not accept commonality unlike its quiddity; and the proof is completed by the necessity of infinite regress. And someone may say: We do not accept that every individuation has a universal quiddity abstracted by the mind from its identity, and the claim of necessity here is not heard, for how, when the rule that every external existent is like that is refuted by them in the case of the Necessary Exalted; rather, every individual of the individuals of individuation is in...
Source pages p. 97

Commentary
This passage presents the second argument against the external existence of individuation: if individuation were an external entity, it would itself require individuation, leading to an infinite regress. The answer given is that 'being an individuation' is a common accident, and the individuals of individuation are distinguished by their own particular essences, not by an additional individuation; the need for another individuation arises only when there is commonality in quiddity, not in accidents. The author (al-Jurjani or the commentator) criticizes this answer: every individual of individuation must have a universal quiddity in the mind, because every external existent does, even if it is a unique species; thus the distinction cannot be by essence alone, and the regress argument stands. He concludes that the proof is complete. Then a counter-objection is introduced: one may deny that every individuation has a universal quiddity, rejecting the necessity claimed, since the rule 'every external existent has a universal quiddity' is violated by the Necessary Being (God) in the philosophers' view; thus the critique fails. The passage ends abruptly at the page break, leaving the counter-objection incomplete.

Key Terms
تعين
الموجود الخارجي
ماهية كلية
تسلسل
عوارض
الواجب تعالى

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Many mistakenly think that the answer 'individuals are distinguished by their essences' fully resolves the infinite regress problem.
Correction: The author shows that even if individuals are distinguished by essences, those essences themselves are universal quiddities that require further individuation, thus the regress remains.

Checkpoint
What is the core of the author's critique against the answer to the second argument?
A) The answer fails because individuation is not an accident.
B) The answer fails because each individuation has a universal quiddity, so distinguishing essence is not sufficient.
C) The answer fails because infinite regress is not a problem.
D) The answer fails because the Necessary Being also has a universal quiddity.

Key Takeaway
The argument that external individuation leads to infinite regress is defended against a counter-answer by showing that every individuation has a universal quiddity, thus the regress is not avoided.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This argument shows that every external existent requires further determination. Your own existence is not self-sufficient but contingent on a greater Determiner. Are you living as if your identity is self-grounded, or do you constantly turn to Allah as the One who defines your reality? What would need to change today for you to live with this awareness?
?
The dialectic about individuation ultimately points to the Necessary Being as the exception. When you engage in deep theological reasoning, do you let it increase your reliance on Allah, or does it remain an intellectual exercise? In the next hour, intentionally use this argument to remind yourself that only Allah is self-determinate and submit one concrete area of your life to His determination.
?
The counter-objection denies that every external existent has a universal quiddity, citing the Necessary Being. If God's essence is beyond universal concepts, have you been trying to 'capture' Him in a mental image or formula? Repent of your mental constructs and commit to knowing Him through His attributes as revealed, not as you imagine.
