Second Argument Against External Individuation: Infinite Regress, Response, and Criticism
Al-Jurjani presents the second argument, its answer, and a criticism.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the infinite regress argument against external individuation, the response that ta'ayyun is an accident, and the criticism that every ta'ayyun still has a quiddity requiring further individuation.

Core Idea
Every external existent needs individuation, but if individuation itself is an external existent, it generates an infinite regress.

This passage presents the second theological argument against the view that individuation (ta'ayyun) exists as an external entity. Al-Jurjani explains the argument, the standard response, and then a criticism of that response from the author of al-Mawaqif. Following the reasoning carefully reveals deep questions about quiddity, accident, and individuation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing it. Then read the translation. Let the overall flow of argument, response, and criticism come through before you interpret.
Notice the three distinct parts: argument, answer, criticism.
2
Identify the infinite regress argument
Find the core logic: if ta'ayyun is an external thing, it itself needs a ta'ayyun, leading to an endless chain.
3
Understand the response
The response says the common concept of ta'ayyun is an accident, not a quiddity, so the regress is avoided because accidents don't require the same kind of individuation.
4
Examine the criticism
The author of al-Mawaqif argues that every instance of ta'ayyun has a universal quiddity distinct from itself, so the regress still applies.
This is the key twist: even if ta'ayyun is an accident, it still has a quiddity that needs individuation.
5
Reflect on the implications
Consider how this debate affects the distinction between essence and existence, and why theologians argued about the nature of individuation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الوجه الثاني : لو كان التعين ( موجوداً) خارجياً (لكان معيناً)، فإن كل موجود خارجي لا بد أن يكون متعيناً في نفسه، (فهو) أي كل واحد من التعين ( مشارك للتعينات ) الأخر ( في كونها تعينا ويمتاز عنها بتعين) آخر يخصه (فيتسلسل)، إذ ننقل الكلام إلى ذلك التعين الآخر. ( وأجيب عنه : بأن كونه تعيناً) أي مفهوم التعين المشترك بين التعينات أمر ( عارض للتعينات)، وهي متمايزة بذواتها المخصوصة ) والمحوج إلى التمايز بتعين زائد هو الاشتراك في الماهية ) دون الاشتراك في العوارض قال المصنف : ( وفيه نظر؛ لأن كل تعين) أي كل فرد من أفراد التعين (فله) ماهية كلية في العقل ضرورة ) ؛ لأن كل موجود في الخارج كذلك، ( سواء كان له ما يشاركه في نوعه أم لا بل انحصر نوعه في شخصه. ) وتعينه غير ماهيته؛ لأنه لا يقبل الشركة بخلاف ماهيته
The second aspect: if individuation were an externally existing thing, it would be individuated, for every externally existing thing must be individuated in itself. (So) each individual of individuation (participates in that it is an individuation and distinguishes itself from others) by another individuation specific to it, thus leading to infinite regress, for we transfer the discussion to that other individuation. And it was answered: that its being an individuation (i.e., the common concept of individuation among individuations) is an accident of the individuations, and they are distinguished by their specific substances, and the need for additional distinction by an extra individuation is due to sharing in quiddity, not sharing in accidents. The author said: 'There is a problem with this; because every individuation (i.e., every individual of individuation) has a universal quiddity in the mind necessarily, because every externally existing thing is like that, whether it has something sharing its species or not, rather its species is confined to its individual. Its individuation is other than its quiddity because it does not admit sharing contrary to its quiddity.'
Source pages p. 98

Commentary
This passage is an objection, answer, and criticism structure. First, the second argument against the existence of individuation (ta'ayyun) as an external entity is presented: if ta'ayyun were an externally existing thing, it would itself need to be individuated. This would require another ta'ayyun to distinguish each ta'ayyun from others, leading to an infinite regress (tasalsul). The response (the answer) is then given: the common concept of ta'ayyun is an accident (arid) that attaches to the individuations, which are already distinguished by their specific substances. The need for an additional ta'ayyun arises only when there is sharing in quiddity (mahiyya), not in accidental attributes. The author (al-Mawaqif's author) then criticizes this response, saying that every individual instance of ta'ayyun necessarily has a universal quiddity that the mind abstracts, since every external existent has such a quiddity. This holds whether or not there are other individuals sharing its species. Thus, the ta'ayyun of each instance is not its quiddity, so the regress argument still applies because the ta'ayyun itself requires a distinguishing factor.

Key Terms
تعين (ta'ayyun)
موجود (mawjud)
ماهية (mahiyya)
عارض (arid)
تسلسل (tasalsul)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Thinking that making ta'ayyun an accident (arid) solves the infinite regress.
Correction: The criticism shows that each ta'ayyun still has a quiddity, which requires further individuation, so the regress persists.

Checkpoint
What is the central problem raised in the second argument against the existence of individuation as an external thing?
A) It leads to a circular definition.
B) It leads to an infinite regress.
C) It contradicts divine simplicity.
D) It makes individuation an accident.

Key Takeaway
Individuation cannot be an external existent because it would require endless further individuation, and even the response that it is an accident fails since each individuation has its own quiddity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Think about the ways you seek to distinguish yourself from others—through achievements, possessions, or roles. This lesson argues that external individuation leads to infinite regress. If your identity depends on such external markers, how can you ever feel truly secure? What one change in your perspective could anchor your sense of self in something that does not require further justification?
?
The passage shows that even the response of making ta'ayyun an accident fails because every individuation has a quiddity that demands a further distinction. Consider: are there aspects of your life where you rely on 'accidental' labels (like job title or social status) to define who you are, while ignoring your unchanging quiddity before Allah? How would your daily actions change if you prioritized your essential self over external distinctions?
?
The criticism reveals that no external individuation can be self-sufficient—it always points beyond itself. In your own life, what 'external individuators' have you assumed would give you lasting definition? Confess one such attachment and commit to releasing it by focusing on the only thing that truly individuates you: your unique soul created by Allah.

The Verbal Nature of the Dispute on Individuation
Al-Jurjani completes the proof, introduces an objection, and concludes the dispute is verbal.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the disagreement between the mutakallimun and philosophers about individuation is essentially verbal, not substantive.

Core Idea
The dispute over individuation is merely verbal; both sides agree it is identical to external identity.

This passage completes the proof of infinite regress and then presents an objection that challenges the universal scope of the rule. The author then resolves the entire debate by showing that the apparent disagreement rests on a misunderstanding of what the philosophers mean by 'existence' of individuation. You will see how careful attention to terms reveals that the two schools are actually saying the same thing.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing, then read the full translation. Notice the flow: completion of proof, objection, and resolution.
The objector's speech starts with 'ولقائل أن يقول'.
2
Identify the objection's core
The objector denies that every individuation has a universal quiddity, using the Necessary Existent as a counterexample. Understand why this challenges the mutakallimun's argument.
The Necessary Existent has no quiddity, so the rule fails for Him.
3
Understand the verbal resolution
The author explains that the mutakallimun's arguments assume individuation is added to quiddity, while the philosophers consider it identical. Since both accept that individuation is the external identity, the dispute is merely verbal.
The key phrase is 'فإذن النزاع لفظي'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويتم الدليل بلزوم التسلسل ولقائل أن يقول : لا نسلم أن كل تعين له ماهية كلية ينتزعها العقل من هويته، ودعوى الضرورة هاهنا غير مسموعة كيف والقاعدة القائلة بأن كل موجود خارجي كذلك منقوض عندهم بالواجب تعالى بل كل فرد من أفراد التعين هو في نفسه بحيث إذا لاحظه العقل لم يمكن له فرض اشتراكه ، ولا تفصيله إلى ماهية قابلة للاشتراك، وأمر زائد عليها مانع من الشركة على قياس تفصيله لأفراد الإنسان. والحق : أن هذين الدليلين الخلفيين للمتكلمين على كون التعين عدمياً مبنيان على كون التعين أمراً منضماً إلى الماهية في الخارج ممتازاً فيه عنها، وقد علمت أنه نفس الهوية الخارجية ذاتاً وجعلاً ووجوداً . وهذا أي كون التعين ممتازاً الماهية في الخارج منضماً إليها بحيث يتحصل منهما هوية مركبة فيه، هو الذي حاول المتكلمون نفيه فإن هذا النفي هو اللازم مما استدلوا به من الوجهين. فإذن النزاع لفظي ، فإن الحكماء يدعون أن التعين أمر موجود، على أنه عين الماهية
And the proof is completed by the necessity of infinite regress. And one may say: we do not grant that every individuation has a universal quiddity that the mind abstracts from its identity, and the claim of necessity here is not listened to, for the rule that every externally existing thing is like that is refuted by them with regard to the Necessary Exalted. Rather, every individual of individuation is in itself such that when the mind observes it, it cannot conceive sharing it, nor analyze it into a quiddity capable of sharing, and an additional thing preventing sharing, analogous to its analysis for individuals of man. The truth is that these two arguments of the mutakallimun for the non-existence of individuation are based on considering individuation as something added to quiddity in the external, distinguished from it. And you have known that it is the same as the external identity in essence, making, and existence. And this – i.e., that individuation is distinguished from quiddity in the external and added to it such that a composite identity results from them – is what the mutakallimun sought to deny. For this denial is necessitated by what they argued from the two aspects. Thus, the dispute is verbal, for the philosophers claim that individuation is an existent thing, but as being identical to quiddity.
Source pages p. 98

Commentary
This passage completes the second argument and then presents a resolution. First, the author states that the proof of infinite regress is complete. Then an objector speaks: he denies that every ta'ayyun has a universal quiddity, arguing that the rule that every external existent has such a quiddity is refuted by the case of the Necessary Existent (al-wajib) – a reference to God, who has no quiddity. Moreover, each individual of ta'ayyun is such that the mind cannot conceive it as being shared or analyzed into a quiddity that admits sharing; it is a unique individual that cannot be universalized, like an individual human that cannot be divided into a universal quiddity and an additional individuator. The author then gives the truth (al-haqq): the mutakallimun's two arguments for the non-existence of ta'ayyun are based on the assumption that ta'ayyun is something added to quiddity in the external, separate from it. But it has been shown that ta'ayyun is identical to the external identity (huwiyya) in essence, making, and existence. Therefore, the mutakallimun's denial of ta'ayyun as something additional is what follows from their arguments, but the philosophers claim that ta'ayyun is an existent thing, meaning it is identical to quiddity, not an extra component. Hence the dispute is merely verbal (lafzi): both parties essentially agree that ta'ayyun is part of the thing's identity, but they express it differently.

Key Terms
دليل خلفي (dalil khalfi)
نزاع لفظي (niza' lafzi)
هوية (huwiyya)
حكماء (hukama')
متكلمون (mutakallimun)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The mutakallimun and philosophers truly disagree about whether individuation exists outside the mind.
Correction: The passage shows the dispute is verbal: the mutakallimun deny a separate individuator, while the philosophers affirm it as identical to essence, so they are not contradicting each other.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the real nature of the disagreement between the mutakallimun and the philosophers (hukama') regarding individuation?
A) It is a factual disagreement about whether individuation exists.
B) It is a verbal dispute based on a false assumption.
C) It is about the definition of quiddity.
D) It cannot be resolved.

Key Takeaway
The dispute over whether individuation is existent or not is merely verbal; both schools agree that it is identical to the external identity of a thing.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Think of a disagreement you have had with another Muslim about a matter of faith. Did it stem from different wording rather than a real difference in belief? Can you now see a path to reconciliation by focusing on shared meaning rather than terms?
?
The mutakallimun and philosophers both sought truth but were trapped by their own formulations. Are there theological phrases you cling to that might be hindering unity with others who hold the same belief in different words? What would it cost you to let go of the exclusive use of that phrase?
?
This lesson shows that clarity on definitions resolved a centuries-old dispute. Where in your own spiritual life are you unclear about what you truly mean by key concepts like 'tawheed' or 'iman'? What one step can you take this week to define your terms more precisely for yourself?

Essence Accepts Sharing, But Not Determination
Introduces the aim and concludes dispute is verbal

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the eleventh aim regarding essence and determination, and why the dispute between mutakallimun and philosophers over determination is merely verbal.

Core Idea
The dispute over determination is verbal because both sides agree on reality.

This lesson introduces a key distinction: essence (mahiyyah) can be shared, but determination (ta'ayyun) cannot. The mutakallimun argue that determination is non-existent, but their proofs assume it is joined to essence externally. The author argues that determination is nothing other than the very identity of the thing, making the dispute merely verbal.

Guided Path
1
Read the aim statement
Read the first sentence: 'al-mahiyyah taqbal al-shirkah duna al-ta'ayyun.' Understand that essence is universal and can be shared, but particular determinations are not part of the essence.
2
Identify the mutakallimun's two proofs
The author refers to two indirect proofs used by the mutakallimun to argue that determination is non-existent. Note that these proofs assume determination is something joined to essence externally.
The proofs are not detailed here; only their assumption is mentioned.
3
Notice the author's correction
The author states that determination is the very identity of the thing in essence, constitution, and existence. It is not an additional element.
4
Grasp the conclusion
Because the mutakallimun assume conjunction and philosophers see identity, the dispute is merely verbal (al-niza' lafzhi). Both sides describe the same external reality.

The Second Observation - The Eleventh Aim: The essence accepts sharing but not determination. Itself such that when the intellect observes it, it cannot posit its sharing, nor its division into an essence capable of sharing and an additional thing preventing sharing, analogous to its division into individuals of man. (And the truth: that these two indirect proofs of the mutakallimun for the non-existentiality of determination are based on the assumption that determination is something joined to the essence in the external world, distinct from it, whereas you have known that it is the very identity externally in essence, constitution, and existence. And this—i.e., determination being distinct from essence in the external world, joined to it such that a composite identity results from them—is what the mutakallimun attempted to negate, for this negation is entailed by what they adduced from the two aspects. Therefore the dispute is verbal, for the philosophers claim that determination is an existent thing, as being identical to essence. What was mentioned is only in possibles, so the correct approach is to suffice with prevention, and what is restricted to the ten categories are types of existents, not their individuals, due to their explicit statement that the point and the unit fall outside, assuming their existence. His statement: (on the analogy etc.) pertains to the negated, not to the negation. His statement: (for the philosophers etc.) How can that be said, when the fact is that they argued for its existentiality by its being a part of the external existent, and they branched on that the explanation of the cause of its non-addition in the Necessary because it entails composition; this is a reconciliation without the consent of the two opponents. Al-Shaykh said in al-Shifa': The animal taken with its accidents is the natural thing, and what is taken in its essence is the nature of which it is said: its existence is prior to the existence of the natural, the priority of the simple over the composite, and it is that whose existence is characterized as the divine existence, because the cause of its existence inasmuch as it is animal is the care of God, and as for its being with matter and accidents of this individual, if it is by the care of God, then it is nature. End quote. And al-Muhaqqiq al-Dawani said: He has repeated in his speech the priority of nature qua nature over the individual nature, so the correct view is to say that the author means that the dispute between the mutakallimun and what is the truth is verbal, indicated by his statement: 'and you have known that it is the very identity,' meaning that determination is existential in the sense that it exists in the external world joined to essence, as you have known from the verification of their doctrine, not that it exists as being identical to essence in the external world, as the commentator (may his soul be sanctified) mentioned, for it is a reconciliation without the consent of the two opponents, as has passed. Because if from it one individual existed, the remaining individuals would be impossible; their impossibility is either for that same essence or for other than it. If for itself, it would be impossible for that necessary individual to exist too, so the Necessary of existence would be impossible of existence—this is the first matter. And if their impossibility is for other than that essence, then in relation to that same essence they are possible, so those individuals impossible in themselves would be unanimously possible—this is the second matter. The answer: that their impossibility is due to their specificities, meaning that what is other than this determination existing in the Necessary cannot combine with that essence because of its demanding a particular determination with a complete demand, and there is no objection in it, and God knows best. His statement: (and you have known that it is the very identity, for if external conjunction were realized, the natural universal would be realized.)
Source pages p. 99

Commentary
This passage is a complex argument within the discussion of determination (ta'ayyun). The author begins by stating the eleventh aim: essence (mahiyyah) accepts sharing (al-shirkah) but not determination—i.e., essence is universal, but particular determinations are not part of the essence. He then refers to the mutakallimun's indirect proofs that determination is non-existent. The author argues that these proofs are based on assuming determination is something joined to essence externally. However, he says the truth is that determination is the very identity (al-huwiyyah) itself. The mutakallimun try to negate this conjunction, so the dispute becomes verbal: philosophers affirm determination as existent and identical to essence. The passage then includes glosses on specific phrases, addressing objections and defending the view that the dispute is verbal, quoting authorities like Ibn Sina and al-Dawani. It concludes with an objection-and-answer about why other individuals are impossible given one determination, and the answer is that impossibility is due to specificities.

Philosophical Clarifications on Determination
Glosses and quotes defending the verbal dispute thesis

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the philosophers' view that determination is existent and identical to essence is defended, and why the dispute remains verbal.

Core Idea
Determination is the very identity of the thing, not an addition.

This lesson delves into the philosophers' position that determination is existent as identical to essence. The author addresses glosses on earlier phrases and quotes Ibn Sina and al-Dawani to show that the dispute is merely verbal. The key is that determination is not a separate component but the essence itself in its concrete existence.

Guided Path
1
Read the philosophers' claim
The passage clarifies that the philosophers claim determination is existent and identical to essence. This is in response to the earlier conclusion that the dispute is verbal.
2
Understand the gloss on the analogy
The author explains that the phrase 'on the analogy' (ala qiyas) pertains to the negated, not to the negation. This resolves a potential misunderstanding about the previous argument.
3
Examine the quotes from Ibn Sina and al-Dawani
Ibn Sina's quote from al-Shifa' discusses the priority of nature over the natural thing. Al-Dawani confirms that the author's intent is to show the dispute is verbal.
4
Conclude with the author's verification
The author restates that determination is existential in the sense of being joined to essence externally, but this 'joining' is not a real composition; it is a conceptual distinction. Thus the dispute remains verbal.

Source Text

المرصد الثاني - المقصد الحادي عشر : الماهية تقبل الشركة دون التعين
نفسه بحيث إذا لاحظه العقل لم يمكن له فرض اشتراكه ، ولا تفصيله إلى ماهية قابلة للاشتراك، وأمر زائد عليها مانع من الشركة على قياس تفصيله لأفراد الإنسان. ( والحق : أن هذين (الدليلين) الخلفيين للمتكلمين على كون التعين عدمياً ( مبنيان على كون التعين أمراً منضماً إلى الماهية في الخارج ممتازاً) فيه ( عنها، وقد علمت أنه نفس الهوية ) الخارجية ذاتاً وجعلاً ووجوداً . ( وهذا ) أي كون التعين ممتازاً الماهية في الخارج منضماً إليها بحيث يتحصل منهما هوية مركبة فيه، (هو الذي حاول المتكلمون نفيه فإن هذا النفي هو اللازم مما استدلوا به من الوجهين. فإذن النزاع لفظي ، فإن الحكماء يدعون أن التعين أمر موجود، على أنه عين الماهية
المذكورة إنما هي في الممكنات، فالصواب الاكتفاء على المنع والمنحصر في المقولات العشر أنواع الموجودات لا أشخاصها لتصريحهم بخروج النقطة والوحدة على تقدير وجودهما. قوله : ( على قياس إلخ ) متعلق بالمنفي لا بالنفي.
قوله : ( فإن الحكماء إلخ) كيف يمكن أن يقال ذلك والحال أنهم استدلوا على وجوديته بجزئيته للموجود الخارجي، وأنهم فرعوا على ذلك بيان علة عدم زيادته في الواجب بأنه يستلزم التركيب، فهذا صلح من غير تراضي الخصمين قال الشيخ في الشفاء : الحيوان مأخوذ بعوارضه هو الشيء الطبيعي، والمأخوذ بذاته هو الطبيعة التي يقال : إن وجودها أقدم من وجود الطبيعي تقدم البسيط على المركب، وهو الذي يخص وجوده بأنه الوجود الإلهي ؛ لأن سبب وجوده بما هو حيوان عناية الله تعالى وأما كونه مع مادة وعوارض هذا الشخص فهو إن كان بعناية الله فهو الطبيعة انتهى وقال المحقق الدواني : ولقد كرر في كلامه تقدم الطبيعة من حيث هي على الطبيعة الشخصية فالصواب أن يقال مراد المصنف أن النزاع بين المتكلمين وبين ما هو التحقيق لفظي، يدل على ذلك قوله : وقد علمت أنه نفس الهوية أي كون التعين وجوديا بمعنى كونه موجوداً في الخارج منضماً إلى الماهية في الخارج على ما علمت من تحقيق مذهبهم، لا أنه موجود على أنه عين الماهية في الخارج، كما ذكره الشارح قدس سره فإنه صلح من غير تراضي الخصمين كما مر .
بسبب
بمعنى
ووجد منها جزئي واحد كانت الجزئيات الباقية ممتنعة فامتناعها إما لنفس تلك الماهية أو لغيرها، فإن كان لنفسها امتنع أن يوجد ذلك الجزئي الواجب أيضاً، فيكون واجب الوجود ممتنع الوجود وهو الأمر الأول، وإن كان امتناعها لغير ذلك الماهية تكون بالنظر إلى نفس تلك الماهية ممكنة، فتكون تلك الجزئيات الممتنعة لذاتها بالاتفاق ممكنة وهو الأمر الثاني. والجواب : أن امتناعها بخصوصياتها، على معنى أن ما سوى هذا التعيين الحاصل في الواجب لا يمكن اجتماعه مع تلك الماهية؛ لاقتضائها تعيناً مخصوصاً اقتضاء تاماً ، ولا محظور فيه والله أعلم . قوله : ( وقد علمت أنه نفس الهوية إذ لو تحقق الانضمام الخارجي لتحقق الكلي الطبيعي
The Second Observation - The Eleventh Aim: The essence accepts sharing but not determination. Itself such that when the intellect observes it, it cannot posit its sharing, nor its division into an essence capable of sharing and an additional thing preventing sharing, analogous to its division into individuals of man. (And the truth: that these two indirect proofs of the mutakallimun for the non-existentiality of determination are based on the assumption that determination is something joined to the essence in the external world, distinct from it, whereas you have known that it is the very identity externally in essence, constitution, and existence. And this—i.e., determination being distinct from essence in the external world, joined to it such that a composite identity results from them—is what the mutakallimun attempted to negate, for this negation is entailed by what they adduced from the two aspects. Therefore the dispute is verbal, for the philosophers claim that determination is an existent thing, as being identical to essence. What was mentioned is only in possibles, so the correct approach is to suffice with prevention, and what is restricted to the ten categories are types of existents, not their individuals, due to their explicit statement that the point and the unit fall outside, assuming their existence. His statement: (on the analogy etc.) pertains to the negated, not to the negation. His statement: (for the philosophers etc.) How can that be said, when the fact is that they argued for its existentiality by its being a part of the external existent, and they branched on that the explanation of the cause of its non-addition in the Necessary because it entails composition; this is a reconciliation without the consent of the two opponents. Al-Shaykh said in al-Shifa': The animal taken with its accidents is the natural thing, and what is taken in its essence is the nature of which it is said: its existence is prior to the existence of the natural, the priority of the simple over the composite, and it is that whose existence is characterized as the divine existence, because the cause of its existence inasmuch as it is animal is the care of God, and as for its being with matter and accidents of this individual, if it is by the care of God, then it is nature. End quote. And al-Muhaqqiq al-Dawani said: He has repeated in his speech the priority of nature qua nature over the individual nature, so the correct view is to say that the author means that the dispute between the mutakallimun and what is the truth is verbal, indicated by his statement: 'and you have known that it is the very identity,' meaning that determination is existential in the sense that it exists in the external world joined to essence, as you have known from the verification of their doctrine, not that it exists as being identical to essence in the external world, as the commentator (may his soul be sanctified) mentioned, for it is a reconciliation without the consent of the two opponents, as has passed. Because if from it one individual existed, the remaining individuals would be impossible; their impossibility is either for that same essence or for other than it. If for itself, it would be impossible for that necessary individual to exist too, so the Necessary of existence would be impossible of existence—this is the first matter. And if their impossibility is for other than that essence, then in relation to that same essence they are possible, so those individuals impossible in themselves would be unanimously possible—this is the second matter. The answer: that their impossibility is due to their specificities, meaning that what is other than this determination existing in the Necessary cannot combine with that essence because of its demanding a particular determination with a complete demand, and there is no objection in it, and God knows best. His statement: (and you have known that it is the very identity, for if external conjunction were realized, the natural universal would be realized.)
Source pages p. 99

Commentary
This passage is a complex argument within the discussion of determination (ta'ayyun). The author begins by stating the eleventh aim: essence (mahiyyah) accepts sharing (al-shirkah) but not determination—i.e., essence is universal, but particular determinations are not part of the essence. He then refers to the mutakallimun's indirect proofs that determination is non-existent. The author argues that these proofs are based on assuming determination is something joined to essence externally. However, he says the truth is that determination is the very identity (al-huwiyyah) itself. The mutakallimun try to negate this conjunction, so the dispute becomes verbal: philosophers affirm determination as existent and identical to essence. The passage then includes glosses on specific phrases, addressing objections and defending the view that the dispute is verbal, quoting authorities like Ibn Sina and al-Dawani. It concludes with an objection-and-answer about why other individuals are impossible given one determination, and the answer is that impossibility is due to specificities.

Key Terms
الكلي الطبيعي
النزاع لفظي
الوجود الإلهي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Dawani, what does the author mean by 'it is the very identity'?
A) Determination is non-existent.
B) Determination is existential in the sense of being joined to essence externally.
C) Determination is a separate part added to essence.
D) Determination is the same as the natural universal.

Key Takeaway
The philosophers' view that determination is existent as identical to essence is defended through a conceptual distinction between nature and natural thing, confirming the dispute is verbal.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If your own identity—your 'determination'—is not a separate addition but the very reality of who you are, how does that challenge the way you think about changing yourself? Are your struggles, sins, or virtues merely accidental, or do they reflect something deeper about your essential self before God?
?
The lesson shows that a long-standing disagreement can be resolved by seeing it as verbal rather than real. Is there a relationship or disagreement in your life where you have been insisting on a difference that might actually be a matter of wording—and what would it cost you to let go and see the shared reality?

Objection and Answer: Impossibility of Other Individuals
Objection and answer about impossibility of other individuals

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the objection that if one individual exists others become impossible, and the answer that impossibility is due to specificities, not the essence.

Core Idea
Impossibility of other individuals is due to their specific determinations, not the essence.

This lesson addresses a key objection: if a given determination exists in the Necessary, why are other determinations impossible? The answer is that each determination entails a specific set of attributes, and the impossibility of others stems from their own specificities, not from the essence itself.

Guided Path
1
Understand the objection
Read the objection: if one individual exists, the remaining individuals would be impossible. This raises the question why.
2
The two alternatives
The passage presents two possibilities: the impossibility is either due to the essence itself or due to something other than the essence. Each leads to a problematic conclusion.
First leads to the Necessary being impossible; second leads to contradiction.
3
The answer
The impossibility is due to their specificities (bikhsusiyyatiha). Other determinations cannot combine with this essence because each determination demands a particular set of attributes.
4
Final remark on natural universal
The passage ends with a reminder that external conjunction would entail the natural universal, which is not the case.
This ties back to the earlier discussion.

Commentary
This passage is a complex argument within the discussion of determination (ta'ayyun). The author begins by stating the eleventh aim: essence (mahiyyah) accepts sharing (al-shirkah) but not determination—i.e., essence is universal, but particular determinations are not part of the essence. He then refers to the mutakallimun's indirect proofs that determination is non-existent. The author argues that these proofs are based on assuming determination is something joined to essence externally. However, he says the truth is that determination is the very identity (al-huwiyyah) itself. The mutakallimun try to negate this conjunction, so the dispute becomes verbal: philosophers affirm determination as existent and identical to essence. The passage then includes glosses on specific phrases, addressing objections and defending the view that the dispute is verbal, quoting authorities like Ibn Sina and al-Dawani. Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The impossibility of other determinations is due to the essence itself being limited.
Correction: The impossibility is due to the specificities of each determination, not the essence. The essence is capable of other determinations, but each determination's specific requirements prevent combination.

Checkpoint
According to the answer, why are other individuals impossible?
A) Because the essence itself prevents them.
B) Because of their specificities (bikhsusiyyatiha).
C) Because they are not possible in themselves.
D) Because the Necessary cannot have multiple determinations.

Key Takeaway
Other determinations are impossible not because the essence excludes them, but because each determination has its own specific requirement that prevents combination.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If the essence of Allah is not limited in any way, yet His specific determinations require that only one exists, what does that say about your own expectations of how He should act? Are you willing to accept that His determinations are complete in themselves, even when they conflict with your desires?
?
The objection implies that limitations arise from specificities, not from the essence. Have you ever attributed a perceived limitation in your life to Allah's essence—such as thinking He is not powerful enough for your situation—when the limitation actually comes from the specific way He has determined your path? How can you realign your thinking?
?
The answer teaches that each determination demands a complete set of attributes. Consider your own life: have you ever felt that specific circumstances (your 'determination') are a barrier to receiving Allah's mercy or guidance? How does this lesson challenge that feeling, showing that it is the nature of determination itself, not a lack in Allah's essence?

Can Essence Cause Determination? The Philosophers' View
Philosophers' thesis on determination by essence with clarifications.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the philosophers' claim that determination (ta'ayyun) is caused by essence, and why it cannot be interpreted as efficient causation.

Core Idea
Essence necessitates determination, but it does not produce it as an efficient cause.

The twelfth aim of this observation examines whether essence can be the cause of determination. The philosophers affirm this, but careful analysis shows that the causality is one of necessary concomitance, not production. The commentator explains the precise meaning and defends against misunderstandings.

Guided Path
1
Read the philosophers' statement
Start by reading the source passage, which presents the philosophers' view that determination is caused by essence. Notice the immediate qualification that it is not efficient causation.
The example of four and evenness is key.
2
Distinguish efficient cause from necessary concomitant
The commentator stresses that essence is not an efficient cause but a necessitating condition. Efficient causation would require precedence, which is impossible here.
Think of how four necessitates evenness without producing it.
3
Examine the condition of 'type confined'
The phrase 'its type is confined' avoids implying a single individual. Essence is taken with the condition excluding determination, so it is not predicated.
This prevents the natural universal from being realized externally.
4
Understand the reply regarding the natural universal
A potential objection is that the natural universal would then exist externally. The commentator offers a possible answer: determination attaches to the individual, not the universal essence.
This leads to the claim that the dispute may be verbal.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المرصد الثاني - المقصد الثاني عشر : التعين إن علل بالماهية ]
بحسب الخارج، ويمتاز عنها في الذهن فقط، والمتكلمون يدعون أنه ليس موجوداً زائداً على الماهية في الخارج منضماً إليها فيه، ولا منافاة بينهما كما ترى .
ومعني
المقصد الثاني عشر : التعين إن علل بالماهية ]
( قال الحكماء) الذاهبون إلى كون التعين وجودياً : ( التعين إن علل بالماهية )
قوله: (إن علل بالماهية بأن كانت الماهية فقط كافيةً في فيضانه من المبدأ المفارق اقتضائها له أنه لا يمكن وجودها بدونه كاقتضاء الأربعة للزوجية لا أن تكون فاعلة له حتى يرد ما يتوهم من أن العلة الفاعلية لا بد أن تتقدم بالوجود والتشخص على معلوله؛ لأن المعدوم والمبهم لا يكون علة للمعين فلو كانت الماهية علة للتشخص يلزم تقدم التشخص على
نفسه.
للتشخص هي
قوله : (انحصر نوعها إلخ) لم يقل انحصرت في الشخص الواحد لأن الماهية المقتضية المأخوذة بشرط لا، أي أن لا يكون التعين مأخوذاً فيه ومنضماً فيه بل خارجاً عنه منضماً إليه، وهي غير محمولة والشخص إنما يقال بالقياس إلى ما يحمل عليه وهي وهي المأخوذة لا بشرط شيء وهو النوع.
في الخارج لا قبلها، فيلزم تحقق الكلي الطبيعي في الخارج. اللهم إلا أن يقال: عروض التعين وما به التعين للمتعين بهذا التعين لا للماهية الكلية، وتقدم المعروض بالوجود ذاتاً لا يقتضي تقدم تعينه أصلاً فلا محذور فيه على أن تقدم التعين على عروض هذه العوارض لا ينافي تأخره عن ذاتها الكافي في كونها ما به التعين، كما ستعرفه .
قوله : ( فإذن النزاع لفظي فإن الحكماء إلخ) هذا صلح من غير تراضي الخصمين كما نقل عن الشارح؛ لأن المتكلمين لا يقولون بوجودية التعين على أنه عين الماهية كما يدل عليه التحرير المذكور قبل. والحق أن النزاع في وجود التعين فرع النزاع في الوجود الذهني، إذ ليس في الخارج أمر متميز عن الماهية منضم إليها في الخارج بل في الخارج، إنما هو الشخص، والعقل يفصله إلى ما به الاشتراك وهو الكلي الطبيعي، وإلى ما به الامتياز وهو التشخص، فإن ثبت الوجود الذهني كان لها ثبوت وإلا فلا وأنت خبير بأن الكلام في وجود التعين في الخارج فلا يكون فرع الوجود الذهني، فليتأمل.
•
قوله: (فإن الحكماء إلخ فيه بحث لأنه إن أراد بكون الماهية علة للتعين فيما انحصر نوعه في شخصه كونها علة موجدة له في الخارج فهو فاسد لاتحادهما في الوجود الخارجي عندهم كما صرح به الآن فلا يعقل كون الماهية موجدة لتعين نفسها . وإن أراد به العلية باعتبار الوجود الذهني فلا وجه له أيضاً؛ لامتناع اقتضاء الماهية الذهنية تشخصها الخارجي، وإلا لزم أن يوجد التعين الخارجي في الذهن ولا يمكن تعدد أفراد تلك الماهية في الذهن أيضاً، فإن قلت : هذا جار في وجود الواجب على رأي المتكلمين . قلت لهم أن يتخلصوا بامتناع التعقل بالكنه
The Second Observation - The Twelfth Aim: Determination if caused by essence. According to the external, and it is distinguished from it only in the mind, and the mutakallimun claim that it is not an existent additional to essence externally joined to it, and there is no conflict between them as you see. And the meaning of the Twelfth Aim: Determination if caused by essence. (The philosophers) who hold that determination is existential said: (Determination if caused by essence). His statement: (If caused by essence, in that the essence alone is sufficient for its emanation from the separate principle, its necessitating it such that its existence cannot be without it, like the necessitation of four for evenness—not that it is an efficient cause of it, so as to ward off what might be imagined that the efficient cause must precede in existence and individuation its effect, because the non-existent and vague cannot be a cause for the determinate; thus if essence were a cause for individuation, the precedence of individuation over itself would be necessary.) For individuation it is. His statement: (its type is confined etc.) He did not say that it is confined to a single individual because the necessitating essence taken with the condition of not—i.e., that determination is not taken into it and joined in it but rather outside it and joined to it—and it is not predicated, and the individual is only said in relation to that which is predicated onto it, and it is what is taken without condition, which is the type. In the external, not before it, so the realization of the natural universal in the external would be necessary. However, it could be said: the occurrence of determination and that by which determination is for that which is determined by this determination, not for the universal essence, and the precedence of the subject in existence essentially does not necessitate the precedence of its determination at all, so there is no objection in it, because the precedence of determination over the occurrence of these accidents does not contradict its posteriority to the essence that suffices as that by which determination is, as you will know. His statement: (Therefore the dispute is verbal, for the philosophers etc.) This is a reconciliation without the consent of the two opponents, as transmitted from the commentator, because the mutakallimun do not say that determination is existential as being identical to essence, as indicated by the aforementioned formulation. The truth is that the dispute over the existence of determination is a branch of the dispute over mental existence, because there is nothing in the external distinct from essence joined to it externally, but rather in the external there is only the individual, and the intellect divides it into that by which it shares—which is the natural universal—and into that by which it is distinguished—which is individuation. If mental existence is established, then it has subsistence; otherwise not. And you are aware that the discussion is about the existence of determination in the external, so it is not a branch of mental existence, so let it be considered. • His statement: (for the philosophers etc.) There is discussion in it, because if what is meant by essence being a cause of determination in cases where its type is confined to its individual is that it is an efficient cause bringing it into existence externally, then it is invalid due to their unity in external existence according to them, as he explicitly stated now, so it is inconceivable that the essence be an efficient cause of its own determination. And if what is meant is the causality with respect to mental existence, there is no basis for it either, because of the impossibility of mental essence necessitating its external individuation, otherwise it would follow that external determination exists in the mind and that multiple individuals of that essence cannot exist in the mind. If you say: this applies to the existence of the Necessary according to the mutakallimun. I say: they can extricate themselves by the impossibility of intellection of the true reality.
Source pages p. 100

Commentary
This passage is a critical examination of the philosophers' claim that essence can be a cause of determination (ta'ayyun). The passage begins by stating the twelfth aim and then presents the philosophers' position: determination is caused by essence in the sense that essence alone suffices for its emanation, similar to the way four necessitates evenness. However, the commentator immediately raises problems. The core difficulty is that if essence were an efficient cause of individuation, it would require precedence of the effect over the cause, which is impossible. The commentator then explains that the philosophers' phrase 'its type is confined' is carefully worded to avoid saying 'confined to a single individual'. They take essence with a condition (bishart la) that excludes determination, so it is not predicated. Then he discusses the consequence that the natural universal would be realized externally, but he offers a possible reply: determination attaches to the determined individual, not to the universal essence. He then returns to the claim that the dispute is verbal, arguing that the mutakallimun do not affirm determination as identical to essence, so the reconciliation is invalid. Instead, he proposes that the dispute over determination is a branch of the dispute over mental existence (al-wujud al-dhihni), because in the external there is only the individual; the intellect divides it into universal and particular. If mental existence is established, then universals have reality; otherwise not. But he notes that the discussion here is about external determination, so this might not apply. Finally, he presents an objection: if essence causes determination externally, it would be self-causation; if mentally, then external individuation would be necessitated by mental essence, which is also problematic. A possible rejoinder for the mutakallimun regarding the Necessary is mentioned.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Determination is efficiently caused by essence.
Correction: The philosophers mean that essence necessitates determination as a necessary concomitant, not that it produces it as an agent.

Checkpoint
What example does the passage give to illustrate the relation between essence and determination?
A) The relation of fire to heat.
B) The necessitation of four for evenness.
C) The relation of a builder to a house.
D) The relation of genus to species.

Key Takeaway
The philosophers affirm that essence necessitates determination, but not as an efficient cause, and this distinction is crucial to avoid absurdities.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The philosophers argue that essence necessitates determination, not as an efficient cause. Examine your own understanding of Allah's attributes: Do you ever unconsciously think of Allah's essence as an efficient cause forcing His actions? How can the distinction between necessitation and efficient causality protect your tawhid from anthropomorphic implications? Commit to one specific way you will remind yourself of this distinction in your daily worship.
?
This lesson reveals that the dispute over determination is tied to the doctrine of mental existence. Reflect on your own assumptions about the reality of concepts: Do you treat mental distinctions (like essence and determination) as mere illusions or as having some reality? How does your position affect how you understand the relationship between Allah's attributes and His essence? Write down a concrete change in how you will think about divine attributes after this lesson.
?
The text warns against a 'reconciliation without consent' of the opponents. In your own intellectual life, have you ever settled for a superficial agreement on a deep theological issue rather than grappling with the substantive differences? What is one area of ʿaqīdah where you have avoided the hard work of understanding opposing views? Resolve to study that issue more deeply this week.

The Verbal Dispute and the Connection to Mental Existence
Final objections and the link to mental existence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the dispute over determination is connected to the doctrine of mental existence, and the final objection against the philosophers' position.

Core Idea
The dispute over determination reduces to the reality of mental existence.

After presenting the philosophers' view, the commentator argues that the dispute is not merely verbal, but rooted in the question of mental existence. He then raises a powerful objection: if essence causes determination externally, it would be self-causation; if mentally, it leads to paradoxes. The mutakallimun have a possible escape regarding the Necessary.

Guided Path
1
Examine the claim of verbal dispute
The commentator notes that someone might think the dispute is verbal, but he rejects this because the mutakallimun do not accept determination as identical to essence.
The reconciliation is without consent of the opponents.
2
Understand the link to mental existence
The commentator proposes that the dispute over determination is a branch of the dispute over mental existence (al-wujud al-dhihni). In the external, there is only the individual; the intellect divides it into universal and particular.
If mental existence is real, then universals have subsistence.
3
Analyze the objection about self-causation
The commentator presents a strong objection: if essence is an efficient cause of determination externally, then since they are identical in existence, it would be self-causation, which is absurd.
This is a logical contradiction.
4
Consider the mental interpretation and the rejoinder
If causality is interpreted mentally, then mental essence would necessitate external individuation, leading to paradoxes. The mutakallimun can escape regarding the Necessary by invoking the impossibility of intellection of the true reality.
This final point is a possible defense.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The philosophers' view is easily refuted by the self-causation argument.
Correction: The self-causation argument only applies if we interpret causality as external efficient causation; the philosophers may intend a different relation.

Checkpoint
What does the commentator say about the interpretation of essence as an efficient cause of determination externally?
A) It is valid if the essence is distinct.
B) It is invalid because it leads to self-causation.
C) It is valid if determination is mental.
D) It is the only interpretation possible.

Key Takeaway
The philosophers' claim fails whether interpreted as external efficient causation or mental causation, but the mutakallimun's position on the Necessary provides an escape from a similar objection.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you reflect on your own identity, do you ever assume that your essence (who you are) fully determines your actions? How does the argument against self-causation in this lesson expose the error in thinking you can be the sole cause of your own choices?
?
Your mental images of Allah are not His true reality. Do you ever treat your conceptual understanding of Allah as if it were the full truth? How does the distinction between mental and external existence protect you from inadvertently limiting your Lord in your mind?
?
The mutakallimun affirm that Allah's true reality cannot be grasped by the mind. Have you ever felt frustrated by this limitation? Or does it humble you and increase your awe? In your worship, how can you turn this intellectual limit into a deeper reliance on revelation and submission?

Determination: Definition and the Philosophers' Causal Argument
Definition and proof of determination's causality by essence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the philosophers' concept of determination as an extra existent caused by the essence in a non-efficient sense, and its consequence that the species is confined to a single individual.

Core Idea
Determination is necessitated by the essence, not produced by it as an efficient cause.

This lesson introduces the central issue of the Twelfth Aim: whether determination is caused by the essence. The philosophers argue it is an extra existent that the essence necessitates, like four necessitates evenness. This leads to the conclusion that the species of such an essence is confined to one individual. We will examine their reasoning and the key terminology.

Guided Path
1
Read the source passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Note the key terms: تعين (determination), ماهية (essence), علة (cause).
The passage is dense; read slowly.
2
Identify the philosophers' claim
Look for the statement that determination is caused by the essence. Understand that they mean a necessitation, not efficient causality.
The example of four and evenness clarifies this.
3
Understand the confinement argument
The philosophers argue that if the essence necessitates determination, then the species (type) of that essence can only have one individual. Why? Because any other determination would require a separate cause.
This is a key proof for the philosophers.
4
Reflect on the significance
Consider how this argument relates to broader issues in theology and philosophy, such as the nature of the Necessary Existent.
This will be developed in later lessons.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المرصد الثاني - المقصد الثاني عشر : التعين إن علل بالماهية بحسب الخارج، ويمتاز عنها في الذهن فقط، والمتكلمون يدعون أنه ليس موجوداً زائداً على الماهية في الخارج منضماً إليها فيه، ولا منافاة بينهما كما ترى .
ومعنى المقصد الثاني عشر : التعين إن علل بالماهية
( قال الحكماء) الذاهبون إلى كون التعين وجودياً : ( التعين إن علل بالماهية )
قوله: (إن علل بالماهية بأن كانت الماهية فقط كافيةً في فيضانه من المبدأ المفارق اقتضائها له أنه لا يمكن وجودها بدونه كاقتضاء الأربعة للزوجية لا أن تكون فاعلة له حتى يرد ما يتوهم من أن العلة الفاعلية لا بد أن تتقدم بالوجود والتشخص على معلولها؛ لأن المعدوم والمبهم لا يكون علة للمعين فلو كانت الماهية علة للتشخص يلزم تقدم التشخص على نفسه.
قوله : (انحصر نوعها إلخ) لم يقل انحصرت في الشخص الواحد لأن الماهية المقتضية المأخوذة بشرط لا، أي أن لا يكون التعين مأخوذاً فيه ومنضماً فيه بل خارجاً عنه منضماً إليه، وهي غير محمولة والشخص إنما يقال بالقياس إلى ما يحمل عليه وهي وهي المأخوذة لا بشرط شيء وهو النوع. في الخارج لا قبلها، فيلزم تحقق الكلي الطبيعي في الخارج. اللهم إلا أن يقال: عروض التعين وما به التعين للمتعين بهذا التعين لا للماهية الكلية، وتقدم المعروض بالوجود ذاتاً لا يقتضي تقدم تعينه أصلاً فلا محذور فيه على أن تقدم التعين على عروض هذه العوارض لا ينافي تأخره عن ذاتها الكافي في كونها ما به التعين، كما ستعرفه .
قوله : ( فإذن النزاع لفظي فإن الحكماء إلخ) هذا صلح من غير تراضي الخصمين كما نقل عن الشارح؛ لأن المتكلمين لا يقولون بوجودية التعين على أنه عين الماهية كما يدل عليه التحرير المذكور قبل. والحق أن النزاع في وجود التعين فرع النزاع في الوجود الذهني، إذ ليس في الخارج أمر متميز عن الماهية منضم إليها في الخارج بل في الخارج، إنما هو الشخص، والعقل يفصله إلى ما به الاشتراك وهو الكلي الطبيعي، وإلى ما به الامتياز وهو التشخص، فإن ثبت الوجود الذهني كان لها ثبوت وإلا فلا وأنت خبير بأن الكلام في وجود التعين في الخارج فلا يكون فرع الوجود الذهني، فليتأمل.
•
قوله: (فإن الحكماء إلخ فيه بحث لأنه إن أراد بكون الماهية علة للتعين فيما انحصر نوعه في شخصه كونها علة موجدة له في الخارج فهو فاسد لاتحادهما في الوجود الخارجي عندهم كما صرح به الآن فلا يعقل كون الماهية موجدة لتعين نفسها . وإن أراد به العلية باعتبار الوجود الذهني فلا وجه له أيضاً؛ لامتناع اقتضاء الماهية الذهنية تشخصها الخارجي، وإلا لزم أن يوجد التعين الخارجي في الذهن ولا يمكن تعدد أفراد تلك الماهية في الذهن أيضاً، فإن قلت : هذا جار في وجود الواجب على رأي المتكلمين . قلت لهم أن يتخلصوا بامتناع التعقل بالكنه
بأن تكون مقتضية لتعينها اقتضاء تاماً إما بالذات، أو بواسطة ما يلزمها، انحصر نوعها في الشخص الواحد الحاصل من الماهية والتعين الذي علل بها، ولم يمكن أن يوجد معها تعين آخر، وإلا انفك عنها التعين الأول فيتخلف المعلول عن علته المستلزمة إياه، هذا إذا كان تعين الماهية زائداً عليها واقتضه الماهية ذلك الاقتضاء، وأما إذا كانت الماهية متعينة بذاتها ممتنعة في نفسها عن فرض الاشتراك فيها، كالواجب تعالى على رأيهم، فلا يتصور هناك تعدد أصلاً، بل هذا أقوى في نفي التعدد
قوله : ( وإلا انفك عنها إلخ) لامتناع اجتماع التعينين.
قوله : ( عن علته المستلزمة إياه ) أشار بقوله : المستلزمة إلى أنه معلول من جنس ما لا ينفك عن العلة فأينما توجد العلة لا بد أن يوجد المعلول، فاندفع ما توهم من أن التخلف إنما يلزم إذا وجدت العلة، ولم يوجد المعلول، لا أن توجد العلة ولم يوجد معها المعلول. قوله : ( هذا إذا كان إلخ ) رد على شارح المقاصد حيث مثل لهذا القسم بالواجب تعالى . قوله : ( على رأيهم قالوا : إن تعينه تعالى عين ماهيته إذ لو كان زائداً عليها لزم تركيب ذات الواجب تعالى .
اللهم إلا أن هذا التخلص إنما هو لبعض القائلين بهذا الامتناع والحق على ما نقل عنه أن هذا الكلام من الفلاسفة مشعر بأن التعين يمتاز عن الماهية في الخارج لكن في العلية على تقدير الامتياز أيضاً بحث ظاهر ، فإن العلية مشروطة بالوجود والتشخص عندهم، والشرط من تتمة العلة باعتبار تأثيرها ، فلا يكون معلولاً لها، اللهم إلا أن يمنع مشروطة العلية بالتشخص، وإن اشترطت بالوجود، غايته استلزام الوجود للتشخص، أما توقفه عليه فلا ؛ حتى يلزم المحذور عليه. وفيه نظر لأن الشيء ما لم يتشخص لم يصر علة لتشخص معين وبمثله أبطل الشارح في موقف الجوهر كون الصورة المطلقة علة للهيولى، ومع هذا فلا بد من القول بوجود الكلي الطبيعي في الخارج، وإلا فما لم يوجد لا يكون علة لوجود شيء آخر على ما زعم الحكماء
قوله : (اقتضاء تاماً الاقتضاء التام بمعنى أن الماهية لو وجدت لم ينفك عنها بحسب ذاتها، وهذا التعين لا ينافي احتياجها في الوجود الخارجي إلى فاعلها حتى ينافي الإمكان . والحاصل : أن الماهية بشرط الوجود الخارجي تقتضي التعين، وأما وجودها فمن الفاعل. بقي فيه بحث آخر وهو أن العلة للتعين فيما ادعى لزوم انحصار النوع في الشخص إذا كان الماهية بشرط الوجود الخارجي، فلم لا يجوز أن تكون كل ماهية مقتضية باعتبار وجوداتها الخاصة تعينات متعددة، والوجودات تلحقها باعتبار العلل والاستعدادات. اللهم إلا أن يقال : لا تعدد للعلل في نفس الأمر وأما الاستعدادات فإنما تتعاقب على المادة، فثبت الاحتياج إليها. وليس حينئذ في إسناد التعينات إلى الماهية باعتبار الوجودات كثير نفع .
The Second Observatory - The Twelfth Aim: Determination (al-ta‘ayyun) if it is caused by the essence (al-māhiyya) according to the external (al-khārij), and it is distinguished from it only in the mind (al-dhihn), and the mutakallimūn claim that it is not an extra existent (mawjūd zā’id) over the essence in the external, conjoined to it therein, and there is no incompatibility between them as you see. The meaning of the Twelfth Aim: Determination if it is caused by the essence. (The philosophers said) those who hold that determination is existential (wujūdī): (Determination if it is caused by the essence). His statement: (If it is caused by the essence) meaning that the essence alone is sufficient in its emanation from the separate principle, its requiring it such that its existence cannot be without it, like the requirement of four for evenness, not that it is an efficient cause for it, so that what is imagined might be refuted: that the efficient cause must precede in existence and individuation (tashakhkhuṣ) its effect, because the non-existent and the indistinct cannot be a cause for the determinate. For if the essence were a cause for individuation, the individuation would have to precede itself. His statement: (Its species is confined, etc.) He did not say confined to one individual (shakhṣ wāḥid) because the requiring essence taken with the condition of non-condition (bi-sharṭ lā), i.e., that determination is not taken into it and conjoined in it, but rather external to it conjoined to it, and it is not predicated, and an individual is only said in relation to what it is predicated upon, and it is taken without condition (lā bi-sharṭ shay’) which is the species. In the external not before it, so the realization of the natural universal (al-kullī al-ṭabī‘ī) in the external follows. However, it may be said: The occurrence of determination and that by which determination is for the determinate by this determination, not for the universal essence, and the priority of the subject (ma‘rūḍ) in existence essentially does not necessitate the priority of its determination at all, so no problem therein, and the priority of determination over the occurrence of these accidents does not contradict its posteriority to the essence itself, sufficient in its being that by which determination, as you will know. His statement: (So then the dispute is verbal, for the philosophers, etc.) This is a reconciliation without the consent of the two opponents as narrated from the commentator; because the mutakallimūn do not affirm the existence of determination as being identical to the essence as indicated by the earlier formulation. And the truth is that the dispute over the existence of determination is a branch of the dispute over mental existence (al-wujūd al-dhihnī), since in the external there is no distinct thing from the essence conjoined to it in the external, rather in the external it is only the individual, and the intellect analyzes it into that by which sharing (i.e., the natural universal) and that by which distinction (i.e., individuation). If mental existence is established, it has subsistence, otherwise not. And you are aware that the discussion is about the existence of determination in the external, so it is not a branch of mental existence, so let it be considered. • His statement: (For the philosophers, etc. has discussion) because if he means by the essence being a cause for determination in what its species is confined to its individual that it is an efficient cause for it in the external, it is false due to their unity in external existence as he stated now, so it is not conceivable that the essence is an efficient cause for its own determination. And if he means causality (al-‘illiyya) with respect to mental existence, there is no justification for it either; due to the impossibility of the mental essence requiring its external individuation, otherwise it would necessitate that external determination exists in the mind and it would not be possible for multiple individuals of that essence in the mind also. If you say: This applies to the existence of the Necessary (al-wājib) according to the mutakallimūn. I say: They can escape by the impossibility of conceptualizing (al-ta‘aqqul) with full comprehension (bi-l-kunh). That it is a require of its determination with a complete requirement either essentially or through what is necessary for it, its species is confined to the single individual resulting from the essence and the determination caused by it, and it is not possible that another determination exists with it, otherwise the first determination would be separated from it, so the effect would be absent from its cause which necessitates it. This is if the determination of the essence is additional to it and the essence requires that requirement. But if the essence is determinate by itself, impossible in itself from supposing sharing in it, like the Exalted Necessary according to their view, no multiplicity is conceivable at all, rather this is stronger in negating multiplicity. His statement: (Otherwise it would be separated from it, etc.) due to the impossibility of two determinations coexisting. His statement: (From its cause which necessitates it) He indicated by his statement 'which necessitates it' that it is an effect of the kind that does not separate from the cause, so wherever the cause exists, the effect must exist. Thus what was imagined that absence only occurs if the cause exists and the effect does not exist, not that the cause exists and the effect does not exist with it. His statement: (This is if, etc.) A refutation of the commentator of al-Maqāṣid where he gave the example of this category with the Exalted Necessary. His statement: (According to their view they said: His determination, exalted, is identical to His essence, for if it were additional to it, composition of the essence of the Exalted Necessary would follow. However, this escape is only for some of those who hold this impossibility. And the truth, as narrated from him, is that this speech of the philosophers indicates that determination is distinguished from the essence in the external, but regarding causality, on the assumption of distinction, there is also an apparent discussion. For causality is conditioned by existence and individuation according to them, and the condition is part of the complete cause with respect to its effect, so it cannot be an effect for it. However, unless it is denied that causality is conditioned by individuation, and even if conditioned by existence, its utmost is that existence necessitates individuation, but its dependence on it is not, so that the problem would follow for him. And there is consideration in it, because a thing as long as it has not been individuated does not become a cause for a specific individuation, and similarly the commentator invalidated in the Station of Substance the absolute form being a cause for hyle. And with this, one must affirm the existence of the natural universal in the external, otherwise what does not exist cannot be a cause for the existence of something else according to the claim of the philosophers. His statement: (A complete requirement) The complete requirement means that if the essence existed, it would not separate from it by its essence, and this determination does not contradict its need in external existence for its agent, so as to contradict contingency. The result: The essence under the condition of external existence requires determination, but its existence is from the agent. There remains another discussion: that the cause for determination in what he claimed necessitates the confinement of species to individual, if the essence is under the condition of external existence, then why is it not permissible that every essence requires, by virtue of its specific existences, multiple determinations, and existences attach to it by virtue of causes and dispositions? However, it may be said: There is no multiplicity of causes in actual fact, and as for dispositions, they only succeed each other upon matter, so the need for them is established. And then there is not much benefit in attributing determinations to the essence by virtue of existences.
Source pages p. 100

Commentary
This passage is a continuous commentary on the Twelfth Aim of the Second Observatory, which asks whether determination (al-ta‘ayyun) is caused by the essence (al-māhiyya). The author first defines the issue: the philosophers hold that determination is an extra existent in the external and is caused by the essence, while the mutakallimūn deny it is an extra existent. The author then explains the philosophers' position in detail. The philosophers argue that determination is caused by the essence in the sense that the essence alone suffices for the emanation of determination from the separate principle, much like the quaternity of four necessitates evenness. This is not efficient causality, as that would require the cause to be existent and individuated before its effect, which would lead to circularity. The commentary then addresses the phrase 'its species is confined' — the philosophers do not say 'confined to one individual' because the essence is taken with the condition of not including determination; the individual is what results from the essence and determination. The discussion then considers an objection: the occurrence of determination is for the determinate, not the universal essence, so no problem. The author then notes the claim that the dispute is verbal, but objects that the mutakallimūn do not affirm determination as identical to the essence. Instead, the dispute hinges on mental existence. The commentary critiques the philosophers' causality: if the essence causes determination in the external, they would be united, so the essence cannot cause its own determination; if in the mind, it cannot cause external individuation. A potential problem with the Necessary Existent is addressed by noting the impossibility of full conceptualization. The explanation of the complete requirement states that if the essence exists externally, it necessitates a single determination, else the effect would be absent from its necessary cause. The commentary notes this applies when determination is additional; for the Necessary Existent, determination is identical to essence, so no multiplicity. Further comments discuss the condition of causality requiring existence and individuation, and the need to affirm the natural universal in the external to avoid circularity. Finally, the author discusses the complete requirement: the essence under the condition of external existence necessitates determination, but existence comes from an agent. A remaining objection about multiple determinations for the same essence is answered by noting that causes do not multiply in actual fact.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the philosophers' claim 'determination is caused by the essence' means the essence efficiently produces determination as a separate effect.
Correction: The philosophers clarify it is a necessitation, like four necessitates evenness, not efficient causality. Efficient causality would require the cause to pre-exist in existence and individuation, leading to circularity.

Checkpoint
According to the philosophers in this passage, what is the relationship between determination and the essence?
A) The essence is an efficient cause that creates determination as a separate existent.
B) The essence necessitates determination such that without it the essence cannot exist, like four necessitates evenness.
C) The essence is identical to determination in the external.
D) The essence receives determination from an external agent.

Key Takeaway
The philosophers argue that determination is necessitated by the essence, not efficiently caused, and this leads to the confinement of the species to a single individual.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you consider your own existence, do you see it as entirely contingent upon God's will, or as a necessary result of some essence? How does the philosophers' view of determination challenge your understanding of God's absolute sovereignty?
?
This passage distinguishes between efficient cause and requirement. In your daily life, do you sometimes attribute outcomes to secondary causes as if they were independent of God? What is one area where you need to reorient your thinking to see God as the sole creator?
?
The author insists the dispute is not merely verbal. Are there theological or existential questions you have dismissed as 'just semantics'? What might it cost you to take such disputes seriously and examine their real implications for your faith?

Logic and Technical Terms

8 min
The First Case: Determination Caused by the Quiddity
Sanusi presents the first case: if the determination of a quiddity is caused by the quiddity itself, it necessitates a single individual.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the first case of determination (ta'ayyun) being caused by the quiddity and why it necessitates a single individual, as well as the distinctions made for self-determined quiddities.

Core Idea
If a quiddity fully necessitates its determination, only one individual can exist.

This lesson introduces the first case in the discussion of determination (ta'ayyun). Sanusi argues that when a quiddity necessitates its own determination completely, the species is limited to one individual. This sets the stage for understanding how multiplicity is impossible in certain cases, including a parallel with the divine essence. The passage also clarifies causal necessitation and addresses potential objections.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Begin by reading the Arabic passage and its literal translation. Notice the key terms and the overall argument structure.
Focus on the phrase 'انحصر نوعها في الشخص الواحد'.
2
Identify the condition and conclusion
Find the condition: the quiddity necessitates its determination with a complete necessitation. Then see the conclusion: the species is restricted to a single individual.
3
Consider the exception for self-determined quiddities
Note that this applies only when determination is additional to the quiddity. For self-determined quiddities like the Necessary, multiplicity is even more impossible.
This connects to the divine attributes debate.
4
Examine the commentary on causality
The commentary clarifies that the cause necessitates the effect such that wherever the cause exists, the effect must exist, refuting a potential misunderstanding.
Also note the refutation of the commentator of al-Maqasid.
5
Reflect on the deeper objections
The text addresses an objection about multiple determinations from the same quiddity via different existences, and responds that causes are not multiple in actual fact.
This shows the sophistication of the argument.
